haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cs-%C4%8Cesko.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d3/Cs-%C4%8Cesko.ogg" class="internal" title="Cs-Česko.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>), is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> to the northeast, and <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> to the east.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The Czech Republic has hilly landscape that covers an area of 78,866 square kilometers (30,450&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) with a mostly temperate <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">continental climate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bohemia" title="Duchy of Bohemia">Duchy of Bohemia</a> under <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Great Moravia</a> in 1002 was formally recognized as an <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Estate" title="Imperial Estate">Imperial State</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> and became <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bohemia" title="Kingdom of Bohemia">a kingdom</a> in 1198.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Path_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Path-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Battle of Mohács">Battle of Mohács</a> in 1526, the whole <a href="/wiki/Lands_of_the_Bohemian_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Lands of the Bohemian Crown">Crown of Bohemia</a> was gradually integrated into the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Monarchy</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Revolt" title="Bohemian Revolt">Bohemian Revolt</a> led to the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_White_Mountain" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of the White Mountain">Battle of the White Mountain</a>, the Habsburgs consolidated their rule. With the dissolution of the Holy Empire in 1806, the Crown lands became part of the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian Empire</a>. </p>
      <p>In the 19th century, the Czech lands became more industrialized, becoming part of the <a href="/wiki/First_Czechoslovak_Republic" title="First Czechoslovak Republic">First Czechoslovak Republic</a> following the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">Austria-Hungary</a> after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">Munich Agreement</a> in 1938, Nazi Germany systematically <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Czechoslovakia" title="German occupation of Czechoslovakia">took control</a> over the Czech lands. <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> was restored in 1945 until 1 January 1993 when it <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Dissolution of Czechoslovakia">dissolved</a> with its constituent states becoming the independent states of the Czech Republic and <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>. The Czech Republic is a member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a>, <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a> and <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">CoE</a>. </p>
      <p>The Czech Republic is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a> with an <a href="/wiki/Developed_country#IMF_advanced_economies" title="Developed country">advanced</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">high income</a> <a href="/wiki/Social_market_economy" title="Social market economy">social market economy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank06_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank06-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a> with a <a href="/wiki/European_social_model" title="European social model">European social model</a>, <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Healthcare in the Czech Republic">universal health care</a> and <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">tuition-free</a> <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Czech_Republic#Tertiary_education" title="Education in the Czech Republic">university education</a>. It ranks 13th in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">UN</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">inequality-adjusted human development</a> and 14th in the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Human_Capital_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="World Bank Human Capital Index">World Bank Human Capital Index</a> ahead of countries such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. It ranks as the <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">11th safest and most peaceful country</a> and 32nd in <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">democratic governance</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Name_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Name of the Czech Republic">Name of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The traditional English name "Bohemia" derives from Latin "Boiohaemum", which means "home of the <a href="/wiki/Boii" title="Boii">Boii</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Gauls" title="Gauls">Gallic</a> tribe). The current English name comes from the <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a> ethnonym associated with the area, which ultimately comes from the Czech word <i>Čech</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-CollinsDictionary_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CollinsDictionary-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-American_Heritage_Dictionary_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American_Heritage_Dictionary-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OxfordDictionary_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OxfordDictionary-25">[25]</a></sup> The name comes from the Slavic tribe (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">Češi, Čechové</i>) and, according to legend, their leader <a href="/wiki/Lech,_%C4%8Cech,_and_Rus" class="mw-redirect" title="Lech, Čech, and Rus">Čech</a>, who brought them to Bohemia, to settle on <a href="/wiki/%C5%98%C3%ADp_Mountain" title="Říp Mountain">Říp Mountain</a>. The etymology of the word <i>Čech</i> can be traced back to the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Slavic" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Slavic">Proto-Slavic</a> root <i>*čel-</i>, meaning "member of the people; kinsman", thus making it <a href="/wiki/Cognate_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cognate (linguistics)">cognate</a> to the Czech word <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%C4%8Dlov%C4%9Bk" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:člověk">člověk</a></i> (a person).<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country has been traditionally divided into three lands, namely <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a> (<i>Čechy</i>) in the west, <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a> (<i>Morava</i>) in the east, and <a href="/wiki/Czech_Silesia" title="Czech Silesia">Czech Silesia</a> (<i>Slezsko</i>; the smaller, south-eastern part of <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">historical Silesia</a>, most of which is located within modern Poland) in the northeast. Known as the <i>lands of the Bohemian Crown</i> since the 14th century, a number of other names for the country have been used, including <i>Czech/Bohemian lands</i>, <i>Bohemian Crown</i>, <i>Czechia</i><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> and the <i>lands of the Crown of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Wenceslaus_I,_Duke_of_Bohemia" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Wenceslaus I, Duke of Bohemia">Saint Wenceslas</a></i>. When the country regained its independence after the dissolution of the <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austro-Hungarian empire</a> in 1918, the new name of <i>Czechoslovakia</i> was coined to reflect the union of the Czech and Slovak nations within one country.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson2012_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson2012-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After Czechoslovakia dissolved in 1992, the Czech Ministry of Foreign Affairs recommended the English name <i>Czechia</i> in 1993, and the Czech government <a href="/wiki/Name_of_the_Czech_Republic#Adoption_of_Czechia" title="Name of the Czech Republic">approved <i>Czechia</i></a> as the official short name in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Geography of the Czech Republic">Geography of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CzechRepublic-geographic_map-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/CzechRepublic-geographic_map-en.svg/220px-CzechRepublic-geographic_map-en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/CzechRepublic-geographic_map-en.svg/330px-CzechRepublic-geographic_map-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/CzechRepublic-geographic_map-en.svg/440px-CzechRepublic-geographic_map-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1949" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CzechRepublic-geographic_map-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Topographic map
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Czech Republic lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/48th_parallel_north" title="48th parallel north">48°</a> and <a href="/wiki/51st_parallel_north" title="51st parallel north">51° N</a> and longitudes <a href="/wiki/12th_meridian_east" title="12th meridian east">12°</a> and <a href="/wiki/19th_meridian_east" title="19th meridian east">19° E</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, to the west, consists of a basin drained by the <a href="/wiki/Elbe" title="Elbe">Elbe</a> (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">Labe</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Vltava" title="Vltava">Vltava</a> rivers, surrounded by mostly low mountains, such as the <a href="/wiki/Krkono%C5%A1e" title="Krkonoše">Krkonoše</a> range of the <a href="/wiki/Sudetes" title="Sudetes">Sudetes</a>. The highest point in the country, <a href="/wiki/Sn%C4%9B%C5%BEka" title="Sněžka">Sněžka</a> at 1,603&nbsp;m (5,259&nbsp;ft), is located here. Moravia, the eastern part of the country, is also hilly. It is drained mainly by the <a href="/wiki/Morava_(river)" title="Morava (river)">Morava River</a>, but it also contains the source of the <a href="/wiki/Oder" title="Oder">Oder</a> River (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">Odra</i>). </p>
      <p>Water from the Czech Republic flows to three different seas: the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. The Czech Republic also leases the <a href="/wiki/Moldauhafen" title="Moldauhafen">Moldauhafen</a>, a 30,000-square-meter (7.4-acre) <a href="/wiki/Lot_(real_estate)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lot (real estate)">lot</a> in the middle of the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> Docks, which was awarded to Czechoslovakia by Article 363 of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>, to allow the landlocked country a place where goods transported down river could be transferred to seagoing ships. The territory reverts to Germany in 2028. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, the Czech Republic belongs to the Central European province of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a>, within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">World Wide Fund for Nature</a>, the territory of the Czech Republic can be subdivided into four <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Western_European_broadleaf_forests" title="Western European broadleaf forests">Western European broadleaf forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_European_mixed_forests" title="Central European mixed forests">Central European mixed forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_mixed_forests" title="Pannonian mixed forests">Pannonian mixed forests</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_montane_conifer_forests" title="Carpathian montane conifer forests">Carpathian montane conifer forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-30">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are four <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national parks</a> in the Czech Republic. The oldest is <a href="/wiki/Krkono%C5%A1e_National_Park" title="Krkonoše National Park">Krkonoše National Park</a> (<a href="/wiki/Man_and_the_Biosphere_Programme" title="Man and the Biosphere Programme">Biosphere Reserve</a>), and the others are <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0umava_National_Park" title="Šumava National Park">Šumava National Park</a> (Biosphere Reserve), <a href="/wiki/Podyj%C3%AD_National_Park" title="Podyjí National Park">Podyjí National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Switzerland" title="Bohemian Switzerland">Bohemian Switzerland</a>. </p>
      <p>The three historical lands of the Czech Republic (formerly some countries of the Bohemian Crown) correspond with the river basins of the <a href="/wiki/Elbe" title="Elbe">Elbe</a> (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">Labe</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Vltava" title="Vltava">Vltava</a> basin for Bohemia, the Morava one for Moravia, and the Oder river basin for Czech Silesia (in terms of the Czech territory). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Czech_Republic_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Czech_Republic_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/250px-Czech_Republic_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Czech_Republic_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/375px-Czech_Republic_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Czech_Republic_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/500px-Czech_Republic_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="765" data-file-height="720"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Czech_Republic_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> types of the Czech Republic 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#3dc6fa; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">Humid continental climate</a>
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#63fd32; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">Oceanic climate</a>
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#007e7e; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">Subarctic climate</a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Czech Republic mostly has a temperate <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>, with warm summers and cold, cloudy and snowy winters. The temperature difference between summer and winter is due to the landlocked geographical position.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Temperatures vary depending on the elevation. In general, at higher altitudes, the temperatures decrease and <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> increases. The wettest area in the Czech Republic is found around <a href="/wiki/B%C3%ADl%C3%BD_Potok_(Liberec_District)" title="Bílý Potok (Liberec District)">Bílý Potok</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jizera_Mountains" title="Jizera Mountains">Jizera Mountains</a> and the driest region is the <a href="/wiki/Louny_District" title="Louny District">Louny District</a> to the northwest of <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>. Another factor is the distribution of the mountains. </p>
      <p>At the highest peak of <a href="/wiki/Sn%C4%9B%C5%BEka" title="Sněžka">Sněžka</a> (1,603&nbsp;m or 5,259&nbsp;ft), the average temperature is −0.4&nbsp;°C (31&nbsp;°F), whereas in the lowlands of the <a href="/wiki/South_Moravian_Region" title="South Moravian Region">South Moravian Region</a>, the average temperature is as high as 10&nbsp;°C (50&nbsp;°F). The country's capital, Prague, has a similar average temperature, although this is influenced by urban factors. </p>
      <p>The coldest month is usually January, followed by February and December. During these months, there is <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">snow</a> in the mountains and sometimes in the cities and lowlands. During March, April, and May, the temperature usually increases, especially during April, when the temperature and weather tends to vary during the day. Spring is also characterized by higher water levels in the rivers, due to melting snow with occasional flooding. </p>
      <p>The warmest month of the year is July, followed by August and June. On average, summer temperatures are about 20–30&nbsp;°C (36–54&nbsp;°F) higher than during winter. Summer is also characterized by rain and storms. </p>
      <p>Autumn generally begins in September, which is still warm and dry. During October, temperatures usually fall below 15&nbsp;°C (59&nbsp;°F) or 10&nbsp;°C (50&nbsp;°F) and <a href="/wiki/Deciduous" title="Deciduous">deciduous</a> trees begin to shed their leaves. By the end of November, temperatures usually range around the freezing point. </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:412px;max-width:412px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:134px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Mala_morava_vojtiskov_morava_valley.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Mala_morava_vojtiskov_morava_valley.jpg/202px-Mala_morava_vojtiskov_morava_valley.jpg" decoding="async" width="202" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Mala_morava_vojtiskov_morava_valley.jpg/303px-Mala_morava_vojtiskov_morava_valley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Mala_morava_vojtiskov_morava_valley.jpg/404px-Mala_morava_vojtiskov_morava_valley.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1667"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Northern Czech landscape during a summer morning
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:134px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Krkono%C5%A1e_mountains_in_winter_2018_04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Krkono%C5%A1e_mountains_in_winter_2018_04.jpg/202px-Krkono%C5%A1e_mountains_in_winter_2018_04.jpg" decoding="async" width="202" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Krkono%C5%A1e_mountains_in_winter_2018_04.jpg/303px-Krkono%C5%A1e_mountains_in_winter_2018_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Krkono%C5%A1e_mountains_in_winter_2018_04.jpg/404px-Krkono%C5%A1e_mountains_in_winter_2018_04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Krkono%C5%A1e" title="Krkonoše">Krkonoše</a> mountains in winter
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The coldest temperature ever measured was in Litvínovice near <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cesk%C3%A9_Bud%C4%9Bjovice" title="České Budějovice">České Budějovice</a> in 1929, at −42.2&nbsp;°C (−44.0&nbsp;°F) and the hottest measured, was at 40.4&nbsp;°C (104.7&nbsp;°F) in <a href="/wiki/Dob%C5%99ichovice" title="Dobřichovice">Dobřichovice</a> in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">rain</a> falls during the summer. Sporadic rainfall is throughout the year (in Prague, the average number of days per month experiencing at least 0.1&nbsp;mm (0.0039&nbsp;in) of rain varies from 12 in September and October to 16 in November) but concentrated rainfall (days with more than 10&nbsp;mm (0.39&nbsp;in) per day) are more frequent in the months of May to August (average around two such days per month).<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Severe <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm" title="Thunderstorm">thunderstorms</a>, producing damaging straight-line winds, <a href="/wiki/Hail" title="Hail">hail</a>, and occasional <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadoes</a> occur, especially during the summer period.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Protected areas of the Czech Republic">Protected areas of the Czech Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Fauna of the Czech Republic">Fauna of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Czech Republic ranks as the 27th most environmentally conscious country in the world in <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> It had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 1.71/10, ranking it 160th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-37">[37]</a></sup> The Czech Republic has four National Parks (<a href="/wiki/%C5%A0umava_National_Park" title="Šumava National Park">Šumava National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krkono%C5%A1e_National_Park" title="Krkonoše National Park">Krkonoše National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cesk%C3%A9_%C5%A0v%C3%BDcarsko_National_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="České Švýcarsko National Park">České Švýcarsko National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Podyj%C3%AD_National_Park" title="Podyjí National Park">Podyjí National Park</a>) and 25 Protected Landscape Areas. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Czech_lands" title="History of the Czech lands">History of the Czech lands</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;max-width:312px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:105px;max-width:105px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:201px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Vestonicka_venuse_edit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Ceramic sculpture" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Vestonicka_venuse_edit.jpg/103px-Vestonicka_venuse_edit.jpg" decoding="async" width="103" height="201" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Vestonicka_venuse_edit.jpg/155px-Vestonicka_venuse_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Vestonicka_venuse_edit.jpg/206px-Vestonicka_venuse_edit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1020" data-file-height="1992"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:203px;max-width:203px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:201px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:The_stone_head_of_a_Celt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Stone Sculpture" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/The_stone_head_of_a_Celt.jpg/201px-The_stone_head_of_a_Celt.jpg" decoding="async" width="201" height="201" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/The_stone_head_of_a_Celt.jpg/302px-The_stone_head_of_a_Celt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/The_stone_head_of_a_Celt.jpg/402px-The_stone_head_of_a_Celt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2652" data-file-height="2652"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          Left: <a href="/wiki/Venus_of_Doln%C3%AD_V%C4%9Bstonice" title="Venus of Dolní Věstonice">Venus of Dolní Věstonice</a> dated to 29,000–25,000 <a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">BCE</a>
          <br>Right: The <a href="/wiki/M%C5%A1eck%C3%A9_%C5%BDehrovice_Head" title="Mšecké Žehrovice Head">stone head of a Celt</a> is among the archaeological collections of the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_(Prague)" title="National Museum (Prague)">National Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Archaeologists have found evidence of prehistoric human settlements in the area, dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> era. </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Classical_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Classical era">classical era</a>, as a result of the 3rd century BC <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> migrations, Bohemia became associated with the <a href="/wiki/Boii" title="Boii">Boii</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rankin2002_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankin2002-39">[39]</a></sup> The Boii founded an <a href="/wiki/Oppidum" title="Oppidum">oppidum</a> near the site of modern Prague.<sup id="cite_ref-(Firm)1997_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-(Firm)1997-40">[40]</a></sup> Later in the 1st century, the Germanic tribes of the <a href="/wiki/Marcomanni" title="Marcomanni">Marcomanni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quadi" title="Quadi">Quadi</a> settled there.<sup id="cite_ref-Salvia2007_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salvia2007-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>–<a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian</a> region settled in the area (their migration was pushed by an invasion of peoples from <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> and Eastern Europe into their area:<sup id="cite_ref-Agnew2004_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agnew2004-42">[42]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avars_(Carpathians)" class="mw-redirect" title="Avars (Carpathians)">Avars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian people">Magyars</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-HahnNadel2014_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HahnNadel2014-43">[43]</a></sup> In the sixth century, the Huns had moved westwards into Bohemia, Moravia, and some of present-day Austria and Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-HahnNadel2014_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HahnNadel2014-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the 7th century, the Frankish merchant <a href="/wiki/Samo" title="Samo">Samo</a>, supporting the Slavs fighting against nearby settled <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Avars</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BartlŠkvarna2002_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BartlŠkvarna2002-44">[44]</a></sup> became the ruler of the first documented Slavic state in Central Europe, <a href="/wiki/Samo%27s_Empire" title="Samo's Empire">Samo's Empire</a>. The principality of <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Great Moravia</a>, controlled by <a href="/wiki/House_of_Mojmir" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Mojmir">Moymir dynasty</a>, arose in the 8th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Champion2005_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Champion2005-45">[45]</a></sup> It reached its zenith in the 9th (during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Svatopluk_I_of_Moravia" title="Svatopluk I of Moravia">Svatopluk I of Moravia</a>), holding off the influence of the Franks. Great Moravia was Christianized, with a role being played by the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> mission of <a href="/wiki/Cyril_and_Methodius" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyril and Methodius">Cyril and Methodius</a>. They codified the <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">Old Church Slavonic</a> language, the first literary and liturgical language of the <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Glagolitic_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Glagolitic alphabet">Glagolitic alphabet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BenedettoDuke2008_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BenedettoDuke2008-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bohemia">Bohemia</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Locator_Lands_of_the_Bohemian_Crown_within_the_Holy_Roman_Empire_(1618).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Locator_Lands_of_the_Bohemian_Crown_within_the_Holy_Roman_Empire_%281618%29.svg/220px-Locator_Lands_of_the_Bohemian_Crown_within_the_Holy_Roman_Empire_%281618%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Locator_Lands_of_the_Bohemian_Crown_within_the_Holy_Roman_Empire_%281618%29.svg/330px-Locator_Lands_of_the_Bohemian_Crown_within_the_Holy_Roman_Empire_%281618%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Locator_Lands_of_the_Bohemian_Crown_within_the_Holy_Roman_Empire_%281618%29.svg/440px-Locator_Lands_of_the_Bohemian_Crown_within_the_Holy_Roman_Empire_%281618%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2769" data-file-height="2524"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Locator_Lands_of_the_Bohemian_Crown_within_the_Holy_Roman_Empire_(1618).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Lands_of_the_Bohemian_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Lands of the Bohemian Crown">Crown of Bohemia</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> (1600). The Czech lands were part of the Empire in 1002–1806, and Prague was the imperial seat in 1346–1437 and 1583–1611.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bohemia" title="Duchy of Bohemia">Duchy of Bohemia</a> emerged in the late 9th century when it was unified by the <a href="/wiki/P%C5%99emyslid_dynasty" title="Přemyslid dynasty">Přemyslid dynasty</a>. Bohemia was from 1002 until 1806 an <a href="/wiki/Imperial_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial State">Imperial State</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PánekTůma2019_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PánekTůma2019-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1212, <a href="/wiki/Ottokar_I_of_Bohemia" title="Ottokar I of Bohemia">Přemysl Ottokar I</a> extracted the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Bull_of_Sicily" title="Golden Bull of Sicily">Golden Bull of Sicily</a> from the emperor, confirming Ottokar and his descendants' royal status; the <a href="/wiki/Duchy" title="Duchy">Duchy</a> of Bohemia was raised to a <a href="/wiki/Realm" title="Realm">Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PánekTůma2019b_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PánekTůma2019b-48">[48]</a></sup> German immigrants settled in the Bohemian periphery in the 13th century.<sup id="cite_ref-PánekTůma2019c_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PánekTůma2019c-49">[49]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongols</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe" title="Mongol invasion of Europe">invasion of Europe</a> carried their raids into Moravia but were defensively defeated at <a href="/wiki/Olomouc" title="Olomouc">Olomouc</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After a series of dynastic wars, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Luxembourg">House of Luxembourg</a> gained the Bohemian throne.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Efforts for a reform of the church in Bohemia started already in the late 14th century. <a href="/wiki/Jan_Hus" title="Jan Hus">Jan Hus</a>'s followers seceded from some practices of the Roman Church and in the <a href="/wiki/Hussite_Wars" title="Hussite Wars">Hussite Wars</a> (1419–1434) defeated five crusades organized against them by <a href="/wiki/Sigismund,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Sigismund, Holy Roman Emperor">Sigismund</a>. During the next two centuries, 90% of the population in Bohemian and Moravian lands were considered <a href="/wiki/Hussites" title="Hussites">Hussites</a>. <a href="/wiki/Petr_Chel%C4%8Dick%C3%BD" title="Petr Chelčický">Petr Chelčický</a> inspired the movement of the <a href="/wiki/Unity_of_the_Brethren" title="Unity of the Brethren">Bohemian Brethren</a> that completely separated from the Catholic Church.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Husit%C3%A9_-_Jensk%C3%BD_kodex.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Painting of battle between mounted knights" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Husit%C3%A9_-_Jensk%C3%BD_kodex.jpg/170px-Husit%C3%A9_-_Jensk%C3%BD_kodex.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Husit%C3%A9_-_Jensk%C3%BD_kodex.jpg/255px-Husit%C3%A9_-_Jensk%C3%BD_kodex.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Husit%C3%A9_-_Jensk%C3%BD_kodex.jpg/340px-Husit%C3%A9_-_Jensk%C3%BD_kodex.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1423" data-file-height="1949"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Husit%C3%A9_-_Jensk%C3%BD_kodex.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Battle between <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Reformation" title="Bohemian Reformation">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Hussites" title="Hussites">Hussites</a> and Catholic <a href="/wiki/Crusade" class="mw-redirect" title="Crusade">crusaders</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Hussite_Wars" title="Hussite Wars">Hussite Wars</a>; Jena Codex, 15th century
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After 1526 Bohemia came increasingly under <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">Habsburg</a> control as the Habsburgs became first the elected and then in 1627 the hereditary rulers of Bohemia. Between 1583 and 1611 Prague was the official seat of the Holy Roman Emperor <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Rudolf II, Holy Roman Emperor">Rudolf II</a> and his court. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Defenestrations_of_Prague" title="Defenestrations of Prague">Defenestration of Prague</a> and subsequent revolt against the Habsburgs in 1618 marked the start of the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>. In 1620, the rebellion in Bohemia was crushed at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_White_Mountain" title="Battle of White Mountain">Battle of White Mountain</a> and the ties between Bohemia and the Habsburgs' hereditary lands in Austria were strengthened. The leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Revolt" title="Bohemian Revolt">Bohemian Revolt</a> were <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_Square_execution" title="Old Town Square execution">executed in 1621</a>. The nobility and the middle class Protestants had to either convert to Catholicism or leave the country.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the "Dark Age" of 1620 to the late 18th century, the population of the <a href="/wiki/Czech_lands" title="Czech lands">Czech lands</a> declined by a third through the expulsion of Czech Protestants as well as due to the war, disease and <a href="/wiki/Famines_in_Czech_lands" title="Famines in Czech lands">famine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The Habsburgs prohibited all Christian confessions other than <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholicism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The flowering of <a href="/wiki/Czech_Baroque_architecture" title="Czech Baroque architecture">Baroque culture</a> shows the ambiguity of this historical period. <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Turks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Tatars</a> invaded Moravia in 1663.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> In 1679–1680 the Czech lands faced the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plague_of_Vienna" title="Great Plague of Vienna">Great Plague of Vienna</a> and an uprising of serfs.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Defenestration-prague-1618.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Defenestration-prague-1618.jpg/170px-Defenestration-prague-1618.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Defenestration-prague-1618.jpg/255px-Defenestration-prague-1618.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Defenestration-prague-1618.jpg/340px-Defenestration-prague-1618.jpg 2x" data-file-width="648" data-file-height="485"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Defenestration-prague-1618.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The 1618 <a href="/wiki/Defenestrations_of_Prague" title="Defenestrations of Prague">Defenestration of Prague</a> marked the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Revolt" title="Bohemian Revolt">Bohemian Revolt</a> against the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">Habsburgs</a> and therefore the first phase of the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There were peasant uprisings influenced by famine.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Serfdom" title="Serfdom">Serfdom</a> was abolished between 1781 and 1848. Several battles of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> took place on the current territory of the Czech Republic. </p>
      <p>The end of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> in 1806 led to degradation of the political status of Bohemia which lost its position of an <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">electorate</a> of the Holy Roman Empire as well as its own political representation in the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Diet_(Holy_Roman_Empire)" title="Imperial Diet (Holy Roman Empire)">Imperial Diet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Bohemian lands became part of the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian Empire</a>. During the 18th and 19th century the <a href="/wiki/Czech_National_Revival" title="Czech National Revival">Czech National Revival</a> began its rise, with the purpose to revive Czech language, culture and national identity. The <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848_in_the_Austrian_Empire" title="Revolutions of 1848 in the Austrian Empire">Revolution of 1848</a> in Prague, striving for liberal reforms and autonomy of the Bohemian Crown within the Austrian Empire, was suppressed.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It seemed that some concessions would be made also to Bohemia, but in the end the Emperor <a href="/wiki/Franz_Joseph_I_of_Austria" title="Franz Joseph I of Austria">Franz Joseph I</a> effected a compromise with Hungary only. The <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Compromise_of_1867" title="Austro-Hungarian Compromise of 1867">Austro-Hungarian Compromise of 1867</a> and the never realized coronation of Franz Joseph as King of Bohemia led to a disappointment of some Czech politicians.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-60">[60]</a></sup> The Bohemian Crown lands became part of the so-called <a href="/wiki/Cisleithania" title="Cisleithania">Cisleithania</a>. </p>
      <p>The Czech Social Democratic and progressive politicians started the fight for universal suffrage. The first elections under <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal male suffrage</a> were held in 1907.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Czechoslovakia" title="History of Czechoslovakia">History of Czechoslovakia</a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Czechoslovakia_I.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Czechoslovakia_I.png/300px-Czechoslovakia_I.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Czechoslovakia_I.png/450px-Czechoslovakia_I.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Czechoslovakia_I.png/600px-Czechoslovakia_I.png 2x" data-file-width="1128" data-file-height="513"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Czechoslovakia_I.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/First_Czechoslovak_Republic" title="First Czechoslovak Republic">First Czechoslovak Republic</a> comprised 27% of the population of the former Austria-Hungary and nearly 80% of the industry.<sup id="cite_ref-Stephen_J._Lee._Page_107._62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stephen_J._Lee._Page_107.-62">[62]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>In 1918, during the collapse of the Habsburg Monarchy at the end of World War I, the independent republic of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>, which joined the winning Allied powers, was created, with <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1_Garrigue_Masaryk" title="Tomáš Garrigue Masaryk">Tomáš Garrigue Masaryk</a> in the lead.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> This new country incorporated the <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Bohemian Crown">Bohemian Crown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/First_Czechoslovak_Republic" title="First Czechoslovak Republic">First Czechoslovak Republic</a> comprised only 27% of the population of the former Austria-Hungary, but nearly 80% of the industry, which enabled it to compete with Western industrial states.<sup id="cite_ref-Stephen_J._Lee._Page_107._62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stephen_J._Lee._Page_107.-62">[62]</a></sup> In 1929 compared to 1913, the gross domestic product increased by 52% and industrial production by 41%. In 1938 Czechoslovakia held 10th place in the world industrial production.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> was the only democracy in Central Europe during the interwar period.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Although the <a href="/wiki/First_Czechoslovak_Republic" title="First Czechoslovak Republic">First Czechoslovak Republic</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a>, it provided certain rights to its minorities. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Praga_11.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Praga_11.jpg/220px-Praga_11.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Praga_11.jpg/330px-Praga_11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Praga_11.jpg/440px-Praga_11.jpg 2x" data-file-width="967" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Praga_11.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Prague during the 1968 <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia">Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Czech territory was <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Czechoslovakia" title="German occupation of Czechoslovakia">occupied by Germany</a>, which transformed it into the <a href="/wiki/Protectorate_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia" title="Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia">Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia</a>. The protectorate was proclaimed part of the Third Reich, and the president and prime minister were subordinated to the Nazi Germany's <i><a href="/wiki/Protector_(title)" title="Protector (title)">Reichsprotektor</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Theresienstadt_concentration_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Theresienstadt concentration camp">One Nazi concentration camp</a> was located within the Czech territory at <a href="/wiki/Terez%C3%ADn" title="Terezín">Terezín</a>, north of Prague. The Nazi <i><a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">Generalplan Ost</a></i> called for the extermination, expulsion, <a href="/wiki/Germanization" class="mw-redirect" title="Germanization">Germanization</a> or enslavement of most or all Czechs for the purpose of providing more <a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">living space</a> for the German people.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> There was <a href="/wiki/Resistance_in_German-occupied_Czechoslovakia" class="mw-redirect" title="Resistance in German-occupied Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovak resistance to Nazi occupation</a> as well as reprisals against the Czechoslovaks for their anti-Nazi resistance. The German occupation ended on 9 May 1945, with the arrival of the Soviet and American armies and the <a href="/wiki/Prague_uprising" title="Prague uprising">Prague uprising</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakian_parliamentary_election,_1946" class="mw-redirect" title="Czechoslovakian parliamentary election, 1946">1946 elections</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Communist Party of Czechoslovakia">Communist Party</a> gained 38%<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> of the votes and became the largest party in the Czechoslovak parliament, formed a coalition with other parties and consolidated power. A <a href="/wiki/1948_Czechoslovak_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1948 Czechoslovak coup d'état">coup d'état</a> came in 1948 and a single party government was formed. For the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Czechoslovakia_(1948%E2%80%931989)" title="History of Czechoslovakia (1948–1989)">next 41 years</a>, the Czechoslovak Communist state is characterized by certain <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a>'s economic and political features.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring" title="Prague Spring">Prague Spring</a> political liberalization was stopped by the 1968 <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia">Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia</a>. Analysts believe that the invasion caused the communist movement to fracture, ultimately leading to the Revolutions of 1989. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Czech_Republic">Czech Republic</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">Velvet Revolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Dissolution of Czechoslovakia">Dissolution of Czechoslovakia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:V%C3%A1clav_Havel_cut_out.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/V%C3%A1clav_Havel_cut_out.jpg/170px-V%C3%A1clav_Havel_cut_out.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/V%C3%A1clav_Havel_cut_out.jpg/255px-V%C3%A1clav_Havel_cut_out.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/11/V%C3%A1clav_Havel_cut_out.jpg 2x" data-file-width="294" data-file-height="336"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:V%C3%A1clav_Havel_cut_out.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Havel" title="Václav Havel">Václav Havel</a>, playwright, former <a href="/wiki/Dissident" title="Dissident">dissident</a>, one of the most important figures in the history of the 20th century. Leader of the <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">Velvet Revolution</a>. The last president of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> and the first president of the Czech Republic.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In November 1989, Czechoslovakia returned to a liberal democracy through the <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">Velvet Revolution</a>. However, Slovak national aspirations strengthened (<a href="/wiki/Hyphen_War" title="Hyphen War">Hyphen War</a>) and on 1 January 1993, the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Dissolution of Czechoslovakia">country peacefully split</a> into the independent <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">countries</a> of the Czech Republic and <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>. Both countries went through economic reforms and <a href="/wiki/Privatisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Privatisation">privatisations</a>, with the intention of creating a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>. This process was largely successful; in 2006 the Czech Republic was recognized by the World Bank as a "developed country",<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank06_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank06-20">[20]</a></sup> and in 2009 the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> ranked it as a nation of "Very High Human Development".<sup id="cite_ref-hdi09_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdi09-71">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From 1991, the Czech Republic, originally as part of Czechoslovakia and since 1993 in its own right, has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">Visegrád Group</a> and from 1995, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>. The Czech Republic joined <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> on 12 March 1999 and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> on 1 May 2004. On 21 December 2007 the Czech Republic joined the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>. Until 2017, either the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Social_Democratic_Party" title="Czech Social Democratic Party">Social Democrats</a> or <a href="/wiki/Civic_Democratic_Party_(Czech_Republic)" title="Civic Democratic Party (Czech Republic)">liberal-conservatives</a> led the government of the Czech Republic. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Government of the Czech Republic">Government of the Czech Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Politics of the Czech Republic">Politics of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:278px;max-width:278px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:136px;max-width:136px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Zeman_M_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Miloš Zeman" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Zeman_M_1.JPG/134px-Zeman_M_1.JPG" decoding="async" width="134" height="187" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Zeman_M_1.JPG/201px-Zeman_M_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Zeman_M_1.JPG/268px-Zeman_M_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1700" data-file-height="2378"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Flag_of_the_President_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/15px-Flag_of_the_President_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Flag_of_the_President_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_President_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Flag_of_the_President_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/30px-Flag_of_the_President_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="526" data-file-height="526"></span> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="President of the Czech Republic">President</a>
           <br><small><a href="/wiki/Milo%C5%A1_Zeman" title="Miloš Zeman">Miloš Zeman</a></small>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:138px;max-width:138px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:A_Babi%C5%A1_Praha_2015.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Andrej Babiš" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/A_Babi%C5%A1_Praha_2015.JPG/136px-A_Babi%C5%A1_Praha_2015.JPG" decoding="async" width="136" height="187" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/A_Babi%C5%A1_Praha_2015.JPG/204px-A_Babi%C5%A1_Praha_2015.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/A_Babi%C5%A1_Praha_2015.JPG/272px-A_Babi%C5%A1_Praha_2015.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2087" data-file-height="2864"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_the_Government_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg" class="image"><img alt="Emblem of the Government of the Czech Republic.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Emblem_of_the_Government_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/15px-Emblem_of_the_Government_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Emblem_of_the_Government_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/23px-Emblem_of_the_Government_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Emblem_of_the_Government_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/30px-Emblem_of_the_Government_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="475" data-file-height="475"></a> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Prime Minister of the Czech Republic">Prime Minister</a>
           <br><small><a href="/wiki/Andrej_Babi%C5%A1" title="Andrej Babiš">Andrej Babiš</a></small>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Czech Republic is a pluralist multi-party <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Parliament of the Czech Republic">Parliament</a> (<i>Parlament České republiky</i>) is bicameral, with the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Chamber of Deputies of the Czech Republic">Chamber of Deputies</a> (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">Poslanecká sněmovna</i>) (200 members) and the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Senate of the Czech Republic">Senate</a> (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">Senát</i>) (81 members).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament#Czech_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">members of the Chamber of Deputies</a> are elected for a four-year term by <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>, with a 5% <a href="/wiki/Election_threshold" class="mw-redirect" title="Election threshold">election threshold</a>. There are 14 voting districts, identical to the country's administrative regions. The Chamber of Deputies, the successor to the <a href="/wiki/Czech_National_Council" title="Czech National Council">Czech National Council</a>, has the powers and responsibilities of the now defunct federal parliament of the former Czechoslovakia. The members of the Senate are elected in single-seat <a href="/wiki/Electoral_district" title="Electoral district">constituencies</a> by two-round <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">runoff voting</a> for a six-year term, with one-third elected every even year in the autumn. This arrangement is modeled on the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">U.S. Senate</a>, but each constituency is roughly the same size and the voting system used is a two-round runoff. </p>
      <p>The president is a formal head of state with limited and specific powers, who appoints the prime minister, as well the other members of the cabinet on a proposal by the prime minister. From 1993 until 2012, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="President of the Czech Republic">President of the Czech Republic</a> was selected by a joint session of the parliament for a five-year term, with no more than two consecutive terms (2x <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Havel" title="Václav Havel">Václav Havel</a>, 2x <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Klaus" title="Václav Klaus">Václav Klaus</a>). Since 2013 the presidential election is direct.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Government of the Czech Republic">Government</a>'s exercise of executive power derives from the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Constitution of the Czech Republic">Constitution</a>. The members of the government are the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Prime Minister of the Czech Republic">Prime Minister</a>, Deputy prime ministers and other ministers. The Government is responsible to the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Chamber of Deputies of the Czech Republic">Chamber of Deputies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Prime Minister of the Czech Republic">Prime Minister</a> is the head of government and wields powers such as the right to set the agenda for most foreign and domestic policy and choose government ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p>
