      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Law of the Czech Republic">Law of the Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Judiciary of the Czech Republic">Judiciary of the Czech Republic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Law enforcement in the Czech Republic">Law enforcement in the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Gun_law_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Gun law in the Czech Republic">Gun law in the Czech Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Self-defence_(Czech_Republic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Self-defence (Czech Republic)">Self-defence (Czech Republic)</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nejvy%C5%A1%C5%A1%C3%AD_spr%C3%A1vn%C3%AD_soud_%C4%8CR_I.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Nejvy%C5%A1%C5%A1%C3%AD_spr%C3%A1vn%C3%AD_soud_%C4%8CR_I.jpg/220px-Nejvy%C5%A1%C5%A1%C3%AD_spr%C3%A1vn%C3%AD_soud_%C4%8CR_I.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Nejvy%C5%A1%C5%A1%C3%AD_spr%C3%A1vn%C3%AD_soud_%C4%8CR_I.jpg/330px-Nejvy%C5%A1%C5%A1%C3%AD_spr%C3%A1vn%C3%AD_soud_%C4%8CR_I.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Nejvy%C5%A1%C5%A1%C3%AD_spr%C3%A1vn%C3%AD_soud_%C4%8CR_I.jpg/440px-Nejvy%C5%A1%C5%A1%C3%AD_spr%C3%A1vn%C3%AD_soud_%C4%8CR_I.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3850" data-file-height="2597"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nejvy%C5%A1%C5%A1%C3%AD_spr%C3%A1vn%C3%AD_soud_%C4%8CR_I.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Seat of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Administrative_Court_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Supreme Administrative Court of the Czech Republic">Supreme Administrative Court of the Czech Republic</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brno" title="Brno">Brno</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Czech Republic is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CabadaWaisová2011_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CabadaWaisová2011-76">[76]</a></sup> with a <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law system</a> based on the continental type, rooted in Germanic legal culture. The basis of the legal system is the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Constitution of the Czech Republic">Constitution of the Czech Republic</a> adopted in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-Kuklík2015_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kuklík2015-77">[77]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Criminal_code" title="Criminal code">Penal Code</a> is effective from 2010. A new <a href="/wiki/Civil_code" title="Civil code">Civil code</a> became effective in 2014. The court system includes district, county and supreme courts and is divided into civil, criminal, and administrative branches. The Czech judiciary has a <a href="/wiki/Triumvirate" title="Triumvirate">triumvirate</a> of supreme courts. The <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Constitutional Court of the Czech Republic">Constitutional Court</a> consists of 15 constitutional judges and oversees violations of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Constitution of the Czech Republic">Constitution</a> by either the legislature or by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Government of the Czech Republic">government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kuklík2015_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kuklík2015-77">[77]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Supreme Court of the Czech Republic">Supreme Court</a> is formed of 67 judges and is the court of highest appeal for most <a href="/wiki/Legal_case" title="Legal case">legal cases</a> heard in the Czech Republic. The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Administrative_Court_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Supreme Administrative Court of the Czech Republic">Supreme Administrative Court</a> decides on issues of procedural and administrative propriety. It also has jurisdiction over certain political matters, such as the formation and closure of political parties, jurisdictional boundaries between government entities, and the eligibility of persons to stand for public office.<sup id="cite_ref-Kuklík2015_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kuklík2015-77">[77]</a></sup> The Supreme Court and the Supreme Administrative Court are both based in <a href="/wiki/Brno" title="Brno">Brno</a>, as is the Supreme Public Prosecutor's Office.<sup id="cite_ref-Kuklík2015_77-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kuklík2015-77">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Foreign relations of the Czech Republic">Foreign relations of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_of_the_Czech_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the Czech Republic">Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Visa_requirements_for_Czech_citizens.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Visa_requirements_for_Czech_citizens.png/220px-Visa_requirements_for_Czech_citizens.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Visa_requirements_for_Czech_citizens.png/330px-Visa_requirements_for_Czech_citizens.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Visa_requirements_for_Czech_citizens.png/440px-Visa_requirements_for_Czech_citizens.png 2x" data-file-width="1353" data-file-height="625"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Visa_requirements_for_Czech_citizens.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Visa-free entry countries for Czech citizens in green, EU in blue (see <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">citizenship of the European Union</a>)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Czech Republic has ranked as <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">one of the safest or most peaceful countries</a> for the past few decades.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> It is a member of the United Nations, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> and is an observer to the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The embassies of most countries with diplomatic relations with the Czech Republic are located in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Consul_(representative)" title="Consul (representative)">consulates</a> are located across the country. </p>
      <p>The Czech passport is <a href="/wiki/Visa_requirements_for_Czech_citizens" title="Visa requirements for Czech citizens">restricted by visas</a>. According to the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Henley_%26_Partners_Visa_Restrictions_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Henley &amp; Partners Visa Restrictions Index">Henley &amp; Partners Visa Restrictions Index</a>, Czech citizens have visa-free access to 173 countries, which ranks them 7th along with <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_Organization" title="World Tourism Organization">World Tourism Organization</a> ranks the Czech passport 24th.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The US <a href="/wiki/Visa_Waiver_Program" title="Visa Waiver Program">Visa Waiver Program</a> applies to Czech nationals. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Prime Minister of the Czech Republic">Prime Minister</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_of_the_Czech_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Czech Republic">Minister of Foreign Affairs</a> have primary roles in setting foreign policy, although the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="President of the Czech Republic">President</a> also has influence and represents the country abroad. Membership in the European Union and NATO is central to the Czech Republic's foreign policy. The <a href="/wiki/Office_for_Foreign_Relations_and_Information" title="Office for Foreign Relations and Information">Office for Foreign Relations and Information</a> (ÚZSI) serves as the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_intelligence" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign intelligence">foreign intelligence</a> agency responsible for <a href="/wiki/Espionage" title="Espionage">espionage</a> and foreign policy briefings, as well as protection of Czech Republic's embassies abroad. </p>
      <p>The Czech Republic has ties with <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Visegrad_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Visegrad Group">Visegrad Group</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> as well as with Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> the United States<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Members_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Members of the European Union">members</a>. </p>
      <p>Czech officials have supported dissenters in <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-democrats_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-democrats-86">[86]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Czech_soldiers_participate_in_exercise_Combined_Resolve_at_the_Joint_Multinational_Readiness_Center_in_Hohenfels,_Germany,_Nov._15,_2013_131115-A-HE359-010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Czech_soldiers_participate_in_exercise_Combined_Resolve_at_the_Joint_Multinational_Readiness_Center_in_Hohenfels%2C_Germany%2C_Nov._15%2C_2013_131115-A-HE359-010.jpg/220px-Czech_soldiers_participate_in_exercise_Combined_Resolve_at_the_Joint_Multinational_Readiness_Center_in_Hohenfels%2C_Germany%2C_Nov._15%2C_2013_131115-A-HE359-010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Czech_soldiers_participate_in_exercise_Combined_Resolve_at_the_Joint_Multinational_Readiness_Center_in_Hohenfels%2C_Germany%2C_Nov._15%2C_2013_131115-A-HE359-010.jpg/330px-Czech_soldiers_participate_in_exercise_Combined_Resolve_at_the_Joint_Multinational_Readiness_Center_in_Hohenfels%2C_Germany%2C_Nov._15%2C_2013_131115-A-HE359-010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Czech_soldiers_participate_in_exercise_Combined_Resolve_at_the_Joint_Multinational_Readiness_Center_in_Hohenfels%2C_Germany%2C_Nov._15%2C_2013_131115-A-HE359-010.jpg/440px-Czech_soldiers_participate_in_exercise_Combined_Resolve_at_the_Joint_Multinational_Readiness_Center_in_Hohenfels%2C_Germany%2C_Nov._15%2C_2013_131115-A-HE359-010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7360" data-file-height="4912"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Czech_soldiers_participate_in_exercise_Combined_Resolve_at_the_Joint_Multinational_Readiness_Center_in_Hohenfels,_Germany,_Nov._15,_2013_131115-A-HE359-010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Army soldiers during an exercise
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Army of the Czech Republic">Army of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Army of the Czech Republic">Czech armed forces</a> consist of the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Land_Forces" title="Czech Land Forces">Czech Land Forces</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Air_Force" title="Czech Air Force">Czech Air Force</a> and of specialized support units. The armed forces are managed by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Czech_Republic)" title="Ministry of Defence (Czech Republic)">Ministry of Defence</a>. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="President of the Czech Republic">President of the Czech Republic</a> is <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">Commander-in-chief</a> of the armed forces. In 2004 the army transformed itself into a fully professional organization and compulsory military service was abolished. The country has been a member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> since 12 March 1999. Defence spending is approximately 1.19% of the GDP (2019).<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The armed forces are charged with protecting the Czech Republic and its allies, promoting global security interests, and contributing to NATO. </p>
      <p>Currently, as a member of NATO, the Czech military are participating in the <a href="/wiki/Resolute_Support_Mission" title="Resolute Support Mission">Resolute Support</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_Force" title="Kosovo Force">KFOR</a> operations and have soldiers in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Atalanta" title="Operation Atalanta">Somalia</a>. The Czech Air Force also served in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The main equipment of the Czech military includes <a href="/wiki/Saab_JAS_39_Gripen" title="Saab JAS 39 Gripen">JAS 39 Gripen</a> multi-role fighters, <a href="/wiki/Aero_L-159_Alca" title="Aero L-159 Alca">Aero L-159 Alca</a> combat aircraft, <a href="/wiki/Mil_Mi-24" title="Mil Mi-24">Mi-35</a> attack helicopters, armored vehicles (<a href="/wiki/Pandur_II" title="Pandur II">Pandur II</a>, <a href="/wiki/OT-64_SKOT" title="OT-64 SKOT">OT-64</a>, <a href="/wiki/OT-90" class="mw-redirect" title="OT-90">OT-90</a>, <a href="/wiki/BMP-2" title="BMP-2">BVP-2</a>) and tanks (<a href="/wiki/T-72" title="T-72">T-72</a> and <a href="/wiki/T-72M4CZ" title="T-72M4CZ">T-72M4CZ</a>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Regions of the Czech Republic">Regions of the Czech Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_of_the_Czech_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="List of districts of the Czech Republic">List of districts of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 2000, the Czech Republic has been divided into <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Regions of the Czech Republic">thirteen regions</a> (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:kraj#Czech" class="extiw" title="wikt:en:kraj"><i>kraje</i>, singular <i>kraj</i></a>) and the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>. Every region has its own elected regional assembly and a regional governor. In Prague, the assembly and presidential powers are executed by the city council and the mayor. </p>
      <p>The older seventy-six <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_of_the_Czech_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="List of districts of the Czech Republic">districts</a> (<i>okresy</i>, singular <i><a href="/wiki/Okres" title="Okres">okres</a></i>) including three "statutory cities" (without Prague, which had special status) lost most of their importance in 1999 in an administrative reform; they remain as territorial divisions and seats of various branches of state administration.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tnone center">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:592px;max-width:592px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:300px;max-width:300px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:169px;overflow:hidden">

          </div>

           Map of the Czech Republic with traditional regions and current administrative regions
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:288px;max-width:288px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:169px;overflow:hidden">

      <p><sup>a</sup> Capital city.<br><sup>b</sup> Office location. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Economy of the Czech Republic">Economy of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Schengenzone.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Schengenzone.svg/220px-Schengenzone.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Schengenzone.svg/330px-Schengenzone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Schengenzone.svg/440px-Schengenzone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="645" data-file-height="690"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Schengenzone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Czech Republic is part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">European Single Market</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, but uses its own currency, the <a href="/wiki/Czech_koruna" title="Czech koruna">Czech koruna</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Czech Republic has a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country#IMF_advanced_economies" title="Developed country">developed</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">high-income</a><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trading_nation" title="Trading nation">export-oriented</a> <a href="/wiki/Social_market_economy" title="Social market economy">social market economy</a> based in services, manufacturing and innovation, that maintains a <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_social_model" title="European social model">European social model</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-An_Ideal-Typical_Perspective_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-An_Ideal-Typical_Perspective-93">[93]</a></sup> The Czech Republic participates in the <a href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">European Single Market</a> as a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and is therefore a part of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_European_Union" title="Economy of the European Union">economy of the European Union</a>, but uses its own currency, the <a href="/wiki/Czech_koruna" title="Czech koruna">Czech koruna</a>, instead of the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>. It has a per capita GDP rate that is 91% of the EU average<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> and is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>. <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">Monetary policy</a> is conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Czech_National_Bank" title="Czech National Bank">Czech National Bank</a>, whose independence is guaranteed by the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Constitution of the Czech Republic">Constitution</a>. The Czech Republic ranks 13th in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">UN</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">inequality-adjusted human development</a> and 14th in <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Human_Capital_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="World Bank Human Capital Index">World Bank Human Capital Index</a>. It was described by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> as "one of Europe's most flourishing economies".<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Czech_Republic&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the country's <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> is $37,370<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> and $22,850 at <a href="/wiki/Real_versus_nominal_value_(economics)" title="Real versus nominal value (economics)">nominal value.</a><sup id="cite_ref-IMFWEOCZ201901_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMFWEOCZ201901-97">[97]</a></sup> According to Allianz A.G., in 2018 the country was an MWC (mean wealth country), ranking 26th in net financial assets.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The country experienced a 4.5% <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">GDP growth</a> in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The 2016 <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a> rate was the lowest in the EU at 2.4%,<sup id="cite_ref-Eurostat_Unemployment_2016_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat_Unemployment_2016-100">[100]</a></sup> and the 2016 poverty rate was the second lowest of OECD members.<sup id="cite_ref-FT_19_October_2016_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT_19_October_2016-101">[101]</a></sup> Czech Republic ranks 24th in both the <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index" title="Global Innovation Index">Global Innovation Index</a> as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Czech_Republic&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> 29th in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">Global Competitiveness Report</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-GCR_2018/19_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCR_2018/19-104">[104]</a></sup> 30th in the <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">ease of doing business index</a> and 25th in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Enabling_Trade_Report" title="Global Enabling Trade Report">Global Enabling Trade Report</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The Czech Republic has a diverse economy that <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_economic_complexity" title="List of countries by economic complexity">ranks 7th</a> in the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Economic_Complexity_Index" title="Economic Complexity Index">Economic Complexity Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Atlas_of_Economic_Complexity_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atlas_of_Economic_Complexity-106">[106]</a></sup> The industrial sector accounts for 37.5% of the economy, while services account for 60% and agriculture for 2.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The largest trading partner for both export and import is <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and the EU in general. Dividends worth CZK 270 billion were paid to the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_ownership" title="Foreign ownership">foreign owners</a> of Czech companies in 2017, which has become a political issue.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The country has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> since 1 May 2004, having abolished border controls, completely opening its borders with all of its neighbors on 21 December 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span></h3> 
      <p>In 2018 the <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_of_the_Czech_Republic#Largest_by_revenue" title="List of companies of the Czech Republic">largest companies</a> by revenue in the Czech Republic were: one of the car automobile manufacturers in Central Europe <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0koda_Auto" title="Škoda Auto">Škoda Auto</a>, utility company <a href="/wiki/%C4%8CEZ_Group" title="ČEZ Group">ČEZ Group</a>, conglomerate <a href="/wiki/Agrofert" title="Agrofert">Agrofert</a>, energy trading company <a href="/wiki/Energetick%C3%BD_a_pr%C5%AFmyslov%C3%BD_holding" class="mw-redirect" title="Energetický a průmyslový holding">EPH</a>, oil processing company <a href="/wiki/Unipetrol" title="Unipetrol">Unipetrol</a>, electronics manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Foxconn_CZ" class="mw-redirect" title="Foxconn CZ">Foxconn CZ</a> and steel producer <a href="/wiki/T%C5%99inec_Iron_and_Steel_Works" title="Třinec Iron and Steel Works">Moravia Steel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Other Czech transportation companies include: <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0koda_Transportation" title="Škoda Transportation">Škoda Transportation</a> (tramways, trolleybuses, metro), <a href="/wiki/Tatra_(company)" title="Tatra (company)">Tatra</a> (heavy trucks, the second oldest car maker in the world), <a href="/wiki/Avia" title="Avia">Avia</a> (medium trucks), <a href="/wiki/Karosa" title="Karosa">Karosa</a> and <a href="/wiki/SOR_Libchavy" title="SOR Libchavy">SOR Libchavy</a> (buses), <a href="/wiki/Aero_Vodochody" title="Aero Vodochody">Aero Vodochody</a> (military aircraft), <a href="/wiki/Let_Kunovice" title="Let Kunovice">Let Kunovice</a> (civil aircraft), <a href="/wiki/Zetor" title="Zetor">Zetor</a> (tractors), <a href="/wiki/Jawa_Moto" title="Jawa Moto">Jawa Moto</a> (motorcycles) and <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cesk%C3%A1_zbrojovka_Strakonice" title="Česká zbrojovka Strakonice">Čezeta</a> (electric scooters). </p>
      <p>Škoda Transportation is the fourth largest <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tramway</a> producer in the world; nearly one third of all trams in the world come from Czech factories.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The Czech Republic is also the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Phonograph_record" title="Phonograph record">vinyl records</a> manufacturer, with <a href="/wiki/GZ_Media" title="GZ Media">GZ Media</a> producing about 6 million pieces annually in <a href="/wiki/Lod%C4%9Bnice_(Beroun_District)" title="Loděnice (Beroun District)">Loděnice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cesk%C3%A1_zbrojovka_Uhersk%C3%BD_Brod" title="Česká zbrojovka Uherský Brod">Česká zbrojovka</a> is among the ten largest <a href="/wiki/Firearm" title="Firearm">firearms</a> producers in the world and five who produce automatic weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">food industry</a> succeeded companies <a href="/wiki/Agrofert" title="Agrofert">Agrofert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kofola" title="Kofola">Kofola</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ham%C3%A9_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hamé (company) (page does not exist)">Hamé</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Energy in the Czech Republic">Energy in the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nuclear.power.plant.Dukovany.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Nuclear.power.plant.Dukovany.jpg/220px-Nuclear.power.plant.Dukovany.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Nuclear.power.plant.Dukovany.jpg/330px-Nuclear.power.plant.Dukovany.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Nuclear.power.plant.Dukovany.jpg/440px-Nuclear.power.plant.Dukovany.jpg 2x" data-file-width="791" data-file-height="586"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nuclear.power.plant.Dukovany.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dukovany_Nuclear_Power_Station" title="Dukovany Nuclear Power Station">Dukovany Nuclear Power Station</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Production of Czech electricity exceeds consumption by about 10 <a href="/wiki/Kilowatt_hour" class="mw-redirect" title="Kilowatt hour">TWh</a> per year, which are exported. <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">Nuclear power</a> presently provides about 30 percent of the total power needs, its share is projected to increase to 40 percent. In 2005, 65.4 percent of electricity was produced by steam and combustion power plants (mostly coal); 30 percent by <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear plants</a>; and 4.6 percent from renewable sources, including hydropower. The largest Czech power resource is <a href="/wiki/Temel%C3%ADn_Nuclear_Power_Station" title="Temelín Nuclear Power Station">Temelín Nuclear Power Station</a>, another <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant" title="Nuclear power plant">nuclear power plant</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Dukovany_Nuclear_Power_Station" title="Dukovany Nuclear Power Station">Dukovany</a>. </p>
      <p>The Czech Republic is reducing its dependence on highly polluting low-grade <a href="/wiki/Lignite" title="Lignite">brown coal</a> as a source of energy. Natural gas is procured from Russian <a href="/wiki/Gazprom" title="Gazprom">Gazprom</a>, roughly three-fourths of domestic consumption and from Norwegian companies, which make up most of the remaining one-fourth. Russian gas is imported via Ukraine, Norwegian gas is transported through Germany. Gas consumption (approx. 100 TWh in 2003–2005) is almost double electricity consumption. South Moravia has small <a href="/wiki/Oil_and_gas_deposits_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Oil and gas deposits in the Czech Republic">oil and gas deposits</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation_infrastructure">Transportation infrastructure</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Transport in the Czech Republic">Transport in the Czech Republic</a>
      </div>
      <p>The road network in the Czech Republic is 55,653&nbsp;km (34,581.17&nbsp;mi) long.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> There are 1,232&nbsp;km of motorways as of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Speed_limits_by_country" title="Speed limits by country">speed limit</a> is 50&nbsp;km/h within towns, 90&nbsp;km/h outside of towns and 130&nbsp;km/h on motorways.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Czech Republic has the densest rail network in the world<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> with 9,505&nbsp;km (5,906.13&nbsp;mi) of tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Of that number, 2,926&nbsp;km (1,818.13&nbsp;mi) is electrified, 7,617&nbsp;km (4,732.98&nbsp;mi) are single-line tracks and 1,866&nbsp;km (1,159.48&nbsp;mi) are double and multiple-line tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cesk%C3%A9_dr%C3%A1hy" title="České dráhy">České dráhy</a> (the Czech Railways) is the main railway operator in the Czech Republic, with about 180&nbsp;million passengers carried yearly. Maximum speed is limited to 160&nbsp;km/h. In 2006 seven Italian <a href="/wiki/Tilting_train" title="Tilting train">tilting trainsets</a> <a href="/wiki/Pendolino" title="Pendolino">Pendolino</a> <a href="/wiki/%C4%8CD_Class_680" title="ČD Class 680">ČD Class 680</a> entered service. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague" title="Václav Havel Airport Prague">Václav Havel Airport</a> in Prague is the main international airport in the country. In 2017, it handled 15 million passengers. In total, the Czech Republic has <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="List of airports in the Czech Republic">46 airports</a> with paved runways, six of which provide international air services in <a href="/wiki/Brno%E2%80%93Tu%C5%99any_Airport" title="Brno–Tuřany Airport">Brno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karlovy_Vary_Airport" title="Karlovy Vary Airport">Karlovy Vary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leo%C5%A1_Jan%C3%A1%C4%8Dek_Airport_Ostrava" title="Leoš Janáček Airport Ostrava">Mošnov</a> (near <a href="/wiki/Ostrava" title="Ostrava">Ostrava</a>), <a href="/wiki/Pardubice_Airport" title="Pardubice Airport">Pardubice</a>, Prague and <a href="/wiki/Kunovice_Airport" title="Kunovice Airport">Kunovice</a> (near <a href="/wiki/Uhersk%C3%A9_Hradi%C5%A1t%C4%9B" title="Uherské Hradiště">Uherské Hradiště</a>). </p>
      <p>Russia, via pipelines through Ukraine and to a lesser extent, Norway, via pipelines through Germany, supply the Czech Republic with liquid and natural gas.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications_and_IT">Communications and IT</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Internet_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Internet in the Czech Republic">Internet in the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Czech Republic ranks in the top 10 countries worldwide with the fastest average internet speed.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> By the beginning of 2008, there were over 800 mostly local <a href="/wiki/Wireless_Internet_service_provider" title="Wireless Internet service provider">WISPs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> with about 350,000 subscribers in 2007. Plans based on either <a href="/wiki/General_Packet_Radio_Service" title="General Packet Radio Service">GPRS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_Data_Rates_for_GSM_Evolution" title="Enhanced Data Rates for GSM Evolution">EDGE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Mobile_Telecommunications_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Mobile Telecommunications System">UMTS</a> or <a href="/wiki/CDMA2000" title="CDMA2000">CDMA2000</a> are being offered by all three mobile phone operators (<a href="/wiki/T-Mobile" title="T-Mobile">T-Mobile</a>, O2, <a href="/wiki/Vodafone" title="Vodafone">Vodafone</a>) and internet provider U:fon. Government-owned <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cesk%C3%BD_Telecom" class="mw-redirect" title="Český Telecom">Český Telecom</a> slowed down broadband penetration. At the beginning of 2004, <a href="/wiki/Local-loop_unbundling" title="Local-loop unbundling">local-loop unbundling</a> began and alternative operators started to offer <a href="/wiki/ADSL" class="mw-redirect" title="ADSL">ADSL</a> and also <a href="/wiki/Symmetric_digital_subscriber_line" title="Symmetric digital subscriber line">SDSL</a>. This and later privatisation of Český Telecom helped drive down prices. </p>
      <p>On 1 July 2006, Český Telecom was acquired by globalized company (Spain-owned) Telefónica group and adopted the new name <a href="/wiki/Telef%C3%B3nica_O2_Czech_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Telefónica O2 Czech Republic">Telefónica O2 Czech Republic</a>. As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Czech_Republic&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, VDSL and ADSL2+ are offered in variants, with download speeds of up to 50 Mbit/s and upload speeds of up to 5 Mbit/s. Cable internet is gaining more popularity with its higher download speeds ranging from 50 Mbit/s to 1 Gbit/s. </p>
      <p>Two <a href="/wiki/Computer_security" title="Computer security">computer security</a> companies, <a href="/wiki/Avast" title="Avast">Avast</a> and <a href="/wiki/AVG_Technologies" title="AVG Technologies">AVG</a>, were founded in the Czech Republic. In 2016, Avast led by <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Baudi%C5%A1" title="Pavel Baudiš">Pavel Baudiš</a> bought rival AVG for <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>1.3&nbsp;billion, together at the time, these companies had a user base of about 400 million people and 40% of the consumer market outside of China.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Avast is the leading provider of antivirus software, with a 20.5% market share.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Tourism in the Czech Republic">Tourism in the Czech Republic</a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Burg_Karlstein_-_Karl%C5%A1tejn_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Burg_Karlstein_-_Karl%C5%A1tejn_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Burg_Karlstein_-_Karl%C5%A1tejn_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Burg_Karlstein_-_Karl%C5%A1tejn_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Burg_Karlstein_-_Karl%C5%A1tejn_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Burg_Karlstein_-_Karl%C5%A1tejn_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Burg_Karlstein_-_Karl%C5%A1tejn_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Burg_Karlstein_-_Karl%C5%A1tejn_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Medieval castle <a href="/wiki/Karl%C5%A1tejn" title="Karlštejn">Karlštejn</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> is the fifth most visited city in Europe after London, Paris, Istanbul and Rome.<sup id="cite_ref-Bremner_2015_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bremner_2015-127">[127]</a></sup> In 2001, the total earnings from tourism reached 118&nbsp;billion <a href="/wiki/Czech_koruna" title="Czech koruna">CZK</a>, making up 5.5% of <a href="/wiki/Measures_of_national_income_and_output" title="Measures of national income and output">GNP</a> and 9% of overall export earnings. The industry employs more than 110,000 people – over 1% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Guidebooks and tourists reporting overcharging by taxi drivers and pickpocketing problems are mainly in Prague, though the situation has improved recently.<sup id="cite_ref-radio_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radio-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-indy_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indy-130">[130]</a></sup> Since 2005, Prague's mayor, <a href="/wiki/Pavel_B%C3%A9m" title="Pavel Bém">Pavel Bém</a>, has worked to improve this reputation by cracking down on petty crime<sup id="cite_ref-indy_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indy-130">[130]</a></sup> and, aside from these problems, Prague is a "safe" city.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> The Czech Republic's crime rate is described as "low".<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>One of the tourist attractions in the Czech Republic<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/Nether_district_V%C3%ADtkovice" class="mw-redirect" title="Nether district Vítkovice">Nether district Vítkovice</a> in Ostrava. </p>
      <p>The Czech Republic boasts <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="List of World Heritage Sites in the Czech Republic">14 UNESCO World Heritage Sites</a>. All of them are in the cultural category. As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Czech_Republic&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, further 18 sites are on the tentative list.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Architectural heritage is an object of interest to visitors – it includes <a href="/wiki/List_of_castles_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="List of castles in the Czech Republic">castles and châteaux</a> from different historical epoques, namely <a href="/wiki/Karl%C5%A1tejn" title="Karlštejn">Karlštejn</a> Castle, <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cesk%C3%BD_Krumlov" title="Český Krumlov">Český Krumlov</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lednice%E2%80%93Valtice_Cultural_Landscape" title="Lednice–Valtice Cultural Landscape">Lednice–Valtice area</a>. There are 12 <a href="/wiki/List_of_cathedrals_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="List of cathedrals in the Czech Republic">cathedrals</a> and 15 churches elevated to the rank of <a href="/wiki/Minor_basilica" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor basilica">basilica</a> by the Pope, calm monasteries. </p>
      <p>Away from the towns, areas such as <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Paradise" title="Bohemian Paradise">Český ráj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Forest" title="Bohemian Forest">Šumava</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Krkono%C5%A1e" title="Krkonoše">Krkonoše</a> mountains attract visitors seeking outdoor pursuits. There is a number of <a href="/wiki/Beer_festival" title="Beer festival">beer festivals</a>. </p>
      <p>The country is also known for its various <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="List of museums in the Czech Republic">museums</a>. <a href="/wiki/Puppeteer" title="Puppeteer">Puppetry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marionette" title="Marionette">marionette</a> exhibitions are with a number of puppet <a href="/wiki/Theatre_festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Theatre festival">festivals</a> throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Aquapalace Praha in <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cestlice" title="Čestlice">Čestlice</a> near Prague, is the biggest <a href="/wiki/Water_park" title="Water park">water park</a> in central Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Demographics of the Czech Republic">Demographics of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> (TFR) in 2015 was estimated at 1.57 children born/woman, which is below the replacement rate of 2.1.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> The Czech Republic's population subsequently has an average age of 42.5 years.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The life expectancy in 2013 was estimated at 77.56 years (74.29 years male, 81.01 years female).<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-139">[139]</a></sup> Immigration increased the population by almost 1% in 2007. About 77,000 people immigrate to the Czech Republic annually.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_people_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Vietnamese people in the Czech Republic">Vietnamese</a> immigrants began settling in the Czech Republic during the Communist period, when they were invited as <a href="/wiki/Guest_workers" class="mw-redirect" title="Guest workers">guest workers</a> by the Czechoslovak government.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> In 2009, there were about 70,000 Vietnamese in the Czech Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Most decide to stay in the country permanently.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to preliminary results of the 2011 census, the majority of the inhabitants of the Czech Republic are <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">Czechs</a> (63.7%), followed by <a href="/wiki/Moravians_(ethnic_group)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moravians (ethnic group)">Moravians</a> (4.9%), <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovaks</a> (1.4%), <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a> (0.4%), <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a> (0.2%) and <a href="/wiki/Silesians" title="Silesians">Silesians</a> (0.1%). As the 'nationality' was an optional item, a number of people left this field blank (26.0%).<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> According to some estimates, there are about 250,000 <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani people</a> in the Czech Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Polish_minority_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Polish minority in the Czech Republic">Polish minority</a> resides mainly in the <a href="/wiki/Zaolzie" title="Zaolzie">Zaolzie</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There were 496,413 (4.5% of population) foreigners residing in the country in 2016, according to the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Statistical_Office" title="Czech Statistical Office">Czech Statistical Office</a>, with the largest groups being <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Ukrainians in the Czech Republic">Ukrainian</a> (22%), <a href="/wiki/Slovaks_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Slovaks in the Czech Republic">Slovak</a> (22%), <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_people" title="Vietnamese people">Vietnamese</a> (12%), <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russian</a> (7%) and <a href="/wiki/Germans_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Germans in the Czech Republic">German</a> (4%). Most of the foreign population lives in Prague (37.3%) and Central Bohemia Region (13.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Czech_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Jews in the Czech Republic">Jewish</a> population of Bohemia and Moravia, 118,000 according to the 1930 census, was annihilated by the Nazi Germans during <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> There were approximately 4,000 Jews in the Czech Republic in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The former Czech prime minister, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Fischer_(politician)" title="Jan Fischer (politician)">Jan Fischer</a>, is of Jewish faith.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the turn of the 20th century, <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> was the city with the third largest Czech population,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> after <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> At the 2010 US census, there were 1,533,826 <a href="/wiki/Czech_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Czech American">Americans of full or partial Czech descent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> </p>
