           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Believers, members of other religions</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:Crimson; width:0.7%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.7%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other religions / Unknown</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:HotPink; width:0.7%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.7%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The Czech Republic has 75%<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> to 79%<sup id="cite_ref-Czech_Statistical_Office_27_February_2014_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Czech_Statistical_Office_27_February_2014-157">[157]</a></sup> of people not declaring any religion or faith in polls and the percentage of convinced <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheists</a> being third highest (30%) behind <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (47%) and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> (31%).<sup id="cite_ref-Global_Index_of_Religion_and_Atheism_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Index_of_Religion_and_Atheism-158">[158]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Czech_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Czech people">Czech people</a> have been historically characterized as "tolerant and even indifferent towards religion".<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Christianization in the 9th and 10th centuries introduced <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholicism</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Reformation" title="Bohemian Reformation">Bohemian Reformation</a>, most Czechs became <a href="/wiki/Hussites" title="Hussites">followers</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jan_Hus" title="Jan Hus">Jan Hus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petr_Chel%C4%8Dick%C3%BD" title="Petr Chelčický">Petr Chelčický</a> and other regional <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformers" title="Protestant Reformers">Protestant Reformers</a>. <a href="/wiki/Taborites" title="Taborites">Taborites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Utraquists" class="mw-redirect" title="Utraquists">Utraquists</a> were <a href="/wiki/Hussite" class="mw-redirect" title="Hussite">Hussite</a> groups. During the <a href="/wiki/Hussite_Wars" title="Hussite Wars">Hussite Wars</a>, Utraquists sided with the Catholic Church. Following the joint Utraquist—Catholic victory, Utraquism was accepted as a distinct form of Christianity to be practiced in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bohemia" title="Kingdom of Bohemia">Bohemia</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> while all remaining Hussite groups were prohibited. After the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a>, some Bohemians went with the <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">teachings of Martin Luther</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Sudeten_Germans" title="Sudeten Germans">Sudeten Germans</a>. In the wake of the Reformation, Utraquist Hussites took a renewed increasingly <a href="/wiki/Anti-Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Catholic">anti-Catholic</a> stance, while some of the defeated Hussite factions were revived. After the <a href="/wiki/Habsburgs" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburgs">Habsburgs</a> regained control of Bohemia, the whole population was forcibly converted to Catholicism—even the Utraquist Hussites. Going forward, Czechs have become more wary and pessimistic of religion as such. A history of resistance to the Catholic Church followed. It suffered a schism with the neo-Hussite <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_Hussite_Church" title="Czechoslovak Hussite Church">Czechoslovak Hussite Church</a> in 1920, lost the bulk of its adherents during the Communist era and continues to lose in the modern, ongoing <a href="/wiki/Secularization" title="Secularization">secularization</a>. Protestantism never recovered after the <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a> was introduced by the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Austrian Habsburgs</a> in 1620. </p>
      <p>According to the 2011 census, 34% of the population stated they had no religion, 10.3% was Catholic, 0.8% was <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> (0.5% <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Church_of_Czech_Brethren" title="Evangelical Church of Czech Brethren">Czech Brethren</a> and 0.4% <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_Hussite_Church" title="Czechoslovak Hussite Church">Hussite</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> and 9% followed other forms of religion both denominational or not (of which 863 people answered they are <a href="/wiki/Neopaganism" class="mw-redirect" title="Neopaganism">Pagan</a>). 45% of the population did not answer the question about religion.<sup id="cite_ref-Czech_Statistical_Office_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Czech_Statistical_Office-6">[6]</a></sup> From 1991 to 2001 and further to 2011 the adherence to Catholicism decreased from 39% to 27% and then to 10%; Protestantism similarly declined from 3.7% to 2% and then to 0.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> The Muslim population is estimated to be 20,000 representing 0.2% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Welfare">Welfare</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Education in the Czech Republic">Education in the Czech Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Healthcare in the Czech Republic">Healthcare in the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Orbispictus.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Orbispictus.JPG/220px-Orbispictus.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Orbispictus.JPG/330px-Orbispictus.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Orbispictus.JPG/440px-Orbispictus.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="571"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Orbispictus.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Orbis_Pictus" title="Orbis Pictus">Orbis Pictus</a></i>, a children's textbook with illustrations<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> published in 1658.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Education in the Czech Republic is compulsory for 9 years and citizens have access to a <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">tuition-free</a> <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Czech_Republic#Tertiary_education" title="Education in the Czech Republic">university education</a>, while the average number of years of education is 13.1.<sup id="cite_ref-Sign_In_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sign_In-164">[164]</a></sup> Additionally, the Czech Republic has a "relatively equal" educational system in comparison with other countries in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Sign_In_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sign_In-164">[164]</a></sup> Founded in 1348, <a href="/wiki/Charles_University" title="Charles University">Charles University</a> was the first university in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>. Other major universities in the country are <a href="/wiki/Masaryk_University" title="Masaryk University">Masaryk University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Technical_University_in_Prague" title="Czech Technical University in Prague">Czech Technical University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palack%C3%BD_University,_Olomouc" class="mw-redirect" title="Palacký University, Olomouc">Palacký University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Performing_Arts_in_Prague" title="Academy of Performing Arts in Prague">Academy of Performing Arts</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Economics,_Prague" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Economics, Prague">University of Economics</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment" title="Programme for International Student Assessment">Programme for International Student Assessment</a>, coordinated by the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>, currently ranks the Czech education system as the 15th most successful in the world, higher than the OECD average.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> The UN <a href="/wiki/Education_Index" title="Education Index">Education Index</a> ranks the Czech Republic 10th as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Czech_Republic&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> (positioned behind <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> and ahead of <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Healthcare in the Czech Republic is similar in quality to other developed nations. The Czech <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a> system is based on a <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance_mandate" title="Health insurance mandate">compulsory insurance model</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Fee-for-service" title="Fee-for-service">fee-for-service</a> care funded by mandatory employment-related insurance plans.<sup id="cite_ref-primary_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-primary-167">[167]</a></sup> According to the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Euro_health_consumer_index" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro health consumer index">Euro health consumer index</a>, a comparison of <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Europe" title="Healthcare in Europe">healthcare in Europe</a>, the Czech healthcare is 13th, ranked behind <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> and two positions ahead of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EHCI_2016_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EHCI_2016-168">[168]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Culture of the Czech Republic">Culture of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:376px;max-width:376px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:92px;max-width:92px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Spring.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Painting of a woman" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Spring.jpg/90px-Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Spring.jpg" decoding="async" width="90" height="177" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Spring.jpg/135px-Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Spring.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Spring.jpg/180px-Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Spring.jpg 2x" data-file-width="508" data-file-height="1000"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:92px;max-width:92px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Summer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Painting of a woman" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Summer.jpg/90px-Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Summer.jpg" decoding="async" width="90" height="179" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Summer.jpg/135px-Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Summer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Summer.jpg/180px-Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Summer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="504" data-file-height="1000"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:92px;max-width:92px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Autumn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Painting of a woman" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Autumn.jpg/90px-Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Autumn.jpg" decoding="async" width="90" height="178" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Autumn.jpg/135px-Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Autumn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Autumn.jpg/180px-Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Autumn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="507" data-file-height="1000"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:92px;max-width:92px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Winter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Painting of a woman" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Winter.jpg/90px-Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Winter.jpg" decoding="async" width="90" height="177" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Winter.jpg/135px-Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Winter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Winter.jpg/180px-Alfons_Mucha_-_1896_-_Winter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="508" data-file-height="1000"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <i>Spring</i>, <i>Summer</i>, <i>Autumn</i> and <i>Winter</i> (1896) by <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Alphonse_Mucha" title="Alphonse Mucha">Alphonse Mucha</a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Venus_of_Doln%C3%AD_V%C4%9Bstonice" title="Venus of Dolní Věstonice">Venus of Dolní Věstonice</a> is the treasure of prehistoric art. <a href="/wiki/Theodoric_of_Prague" class="mw-redirect" title="Theodoric of Prague">Theodoric of Prague</a> was a painter in the Gothic era who decorated the castle Karlstejn. In the Baroque era, there were <a href="/wiki/Wenceslaus_Hollar" title="Wenceslaus Hollar">Wenceslaus Hollar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Kupeck%C3%BD" title="Jan Kupecký">Jan Kupecký</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karel_%C5%A0kr%C3%A9ta" title="Karel Škréta">Karel Škréta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anton_Raphael_Mengs" title="Anton Raphael Mengs">Anton Raphael Mengs</a> or <a href="/wiki/Petr_Brandl" title="Petr Brandl">Petr Brandl</a>, sculptors <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Braun" title="Matthias Braun">Matthias Braun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Brokoff" title="Ferdinand Brokoff">Ferdinand Brokoff</a>. In the first half of the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Josef_M%C3%A1nes" title="Josef Mánes">Josef Mánes</a> joined the romantic movement. In the second half of the 19th century had the main say the so-called "National Theatre generation": sculptor <a href="/wiki/Josef_V%C3%A1clav_Myslbek" title="Josef Václav Myslbek">Josef Václav Myslbek</a> and painters <a href="/wiki/Mikol%C3%A1%C5%A1_Ale%C5%A1" title="Mikoláš Aleš">Mikoláš Aleš</a>, <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Bro%C5%BE%C3%ADk" title="Václav Brožík">Václav Brožík</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vojt%C4%9Bch_Hynais" title="Vojtěch Hynais">Vojtěch Hynais</a> or <a href="/wiki/Julius_Ma%C5%99%C3%A1k" title="Julius Mařák">Julius Mařák</a>. At the end of the century came a wave of <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a>. Alfons Mucha became the main representative. He is known for <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> posters and his cycle of 20 large canvases named <a href="/wiki/The_Slav_Epic" title="The Slav Epic">the Slav Epic</a>, which depicts the history of Czechs and other <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a>. </p>
      <p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Czech_Republic&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/The_Slav_Epic" title="The Slav Epic">the Slav Epic</a> can be seen in the Veletržní Palace of the <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_in_Prague" class="mw-redirect" title="National Gallery in Prague">National Gallery in Prague</a>, which manages the largest collection of art in the Czech Republic. <a href="/wiki/Max_%C5%A0vabinsk%C3%BD" title="Max Švabinský">Max Švabinský</a> was another Art nouveau painter. The 20th century brought avant-garde revolution. In the Czech lands mainly expressionist and cubist: <a href="/wiki/Josef_%C4%8Capek" title="Josef Čapek">Josef Čapek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emil_Filla" title="Emil Filla">Emil Filla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bohumil_Kubi%C5%A1ta" title="Bohumil Kubišta">Bohumil Kubišta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Zrzav%C3%BD" title="Jan Zrzavý">Jan Zrzavý</a>. Surrealism emerged particularly in the work of <a href="/wiki/Toyen" title="Toyen">Toyen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josef_%C5%A0%C3%ADma" title="Josef Šíma">Josef Šíma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karel_Teige" title="Karel Teige">Karel Teige</a>. In the world, however, he pushed mainly <a href="/wiki/Franti%C5%A1ek_Kupka" title="František Kupka">František Kupka</a>, a pioneer of abstract painting. As illustrators and cartoonists in the first half of the 20th century gained fame <a href="/wiki/Josef_Lada" title="Josef Lada">Josef Lada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zden%C4%9Bk_Burian" title="Zdeněk Burian">Zdeněk Burian</a> or <a href="/wiki/Emil_Orl%C3%ADk" title="Emil Orlík">Emil Orlík</a>. Art photography has become a new field (<a href="/wiki/Franti%C5%A1ek_Drtikol" title="František Drtikol">František Drtikol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josef_Sudek" title="Josef Sudek">Josef Sudek</a>, later <a href="/wiki/Jan_Saudek" title="Jan Saudek">Jan Saudek</a> or <a href="/wiki/Josef_Koudelka" title="Josef Koudelka">Josef Koudelka</a>). </p>
      <p>The Czech Republic is known for its individually made, mouth blown and decorated <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_glass" title="Bohemian glass">Bohemian glass</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Czech_architecture" title="Czech architecture">Czech architecture</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MLS_Kou%C5%99im,_podst%C3%A1vkov%C3%BD_d%C5%AFm_z_J%C3%ADlov%C3%A9ho_u_D%C4%9B%C4%8D%C3%ADna.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/MLS_Kou%C5%99im%2C_podst%C3%A1vkov%C3%BD_d%C5%AFm_z_J%C3%ADlov%C3%A9ho_u_D%C4%9B%C4%8D%C3%ADna.jpg/220px-MLS_Kou%C5%99im%2C_podst%C3%A1vkov%C3%BD_d%C5%AFm_z_J%C3%ADlov%C3%A9ho_u_D%C4%9B%C4%8D%C3%ADna.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/MLS_Kou%C5%99im%2C_podst%C3%A1vkov%C3%BD_d%C5%AFm_z_J%C3%ADlov%C3%A9ho_u_D%C4%9B%C4%8D%C3%ADna.jpg/330px-MLS_Kou%C5%99im%2C_podst%C3%A1vkov%C3%BD_d%C5%AFm_z_J%C3%ADlov%C3%A9ho_u_D%C4%9B%C4%8D%C3%ADna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/MLS_Kou%C5%99im%2C_podst%C3%A1vkov%C3%BD_d%C5%AFm_z_J%C3%ADlov%C3%A9ho_u_D%C4%9B%C4%8D%C3%ADna.jpg/440px-MLS_Kou%C5%99im%2C_podst%C3%A1vkov%C3%BD_d%C5%AFm_z_J%C3%ADlov%C3%A9ho_u_D%C4%9B%C4%8D%C3%ADna.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2984" data-file-height="1765"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MLS_Kou%C5%99im,_podst%C3%A1vkov%C3%BD_d%C5%AFm_z_J%C3%ADlov%C3%A9ho_u_D%C4%9B%C4%8D%C3%ADna.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>18th century farmhouse
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Prague_07-2016_View_from_Old_Town_Hall_Tower_img3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Prague_07-2016_View_from_Old_Town_Hall_Tower_img3.jpg/220px-Prague_07-2016_View_from_Old_Town_Hall_Tower_img3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Prague_07-2016_View_from_Old_Town_Hall_Tower_img3.jpg/330px-Prague_07-2016_View_from_Old_Town_Hall_Tower_img3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Prague_07-2016_View_from_Old_Town_Hall_Tower_img3.jpg/440px-Prague_07-2016_View_from_Old_Town_Hall_Tower_img3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4433" data-file-height="2771"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Prague_07-2016_View_from_Old_Town_Hall_Tower_img3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Historic center of Prague
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The earliest preserved stone buildings in Bohemia and Moravia date back to the time of the <a href="/wiki/Christianization" title="Christianization">Christianization</a> in the 9th and 10th century. Since the Middle Ages, the Czech lands have been using the same architectural styles as most of <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western</a> and Central Europe. The oldest still standing churches were built in the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque style</a>. During the 13th century it was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Gothic_architecture" title="Czech Gothic architecture">Gothic style</a>. In the 14th century Emperor Charles IV invited to his court in Prague architects from France and Germany, <a href="/wiki/Matthias_of_Arras" title="Matthias of Arras">Matthias of Arras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Parler" title="Peter Parler">Peter Parler</a>. During the Middle Ages, some fortified castles were built by the king and aristocracy, as well as some monasteries. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">Renaissance style</a> penetrated the Bohemian Crown in the late 15th century when the older Gothic style started to be mixed with Renaissance elements. An example of the pure Renaissance architecture in Bohemia is the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Anne%27s_Summer_Palace" title="Queen Anne's Summer Palace">Queen Anne's Summer Palace</a>, which was situated in the garden of <a href="/wiki/Prague_Castle" title="Prague Castle">Prague Castle</a>. Evidence of the general reception of the Renaissance in Bohemia, involving an influx of Italian architects, can be found in spacious châteaux with arcade courtyards and geometrically arranged gardens.<sup id="cite_ref-architecture_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-architecture-169">[169]</a></sup> Emphasis was placed on comfort, and buildings that were built for entertainment purposes also appeared.<sup id="cite_ref-czecharchitecture_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-czecharchitecture-170">[170]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 17th century, the Baroque style spread throughout the Crown of Bohemia.<sup id="cite_ref-kotalik_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kotalik-171">[171]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 18th century Bohemia produced an architectural peculiarity – the <i>Baroque Gothic style</i>, a synthesis of the Gothic and Baroque styles.<sup id="cite_ref-architecture_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-architecture-169">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the 19th century stands the <a href="/wiki/Revival_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Revival architecture">revival architectural styles</a>. Some churches were restored to their presumed medieval appearance and there were constructed buildings in the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_Revival_architecture" title="Romanesque Revival architecture">Neo-Romanesque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Neo-Gothic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Revival_architecture" title="Renaissance Revival architecture">Neo-Renaissance</a> styles. At the turn of the 19th and 20th centuries the new art style appeared in the Czech lands – <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a>. </p>
      <p>Bohemia contributed an unusual style to the world's architectural heritage when Czech architects attempted to transpose the <a href="/wiki/Cubism" title="Cubism">Cubism</a> of painting and sculpture into architecture. </p>
      <p>Between World Wars I and II, <a href="/wiki/Functionalism_(architecture)" title="Functionalism (architecture)">Functionalism</a>, with its sober, progressive forms, took over as the main architectural style.<sup id="cite_ref-architecture_169-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-architecture-169">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After World War II and the Communist coup in 1948, art in Czechoslovakia became Soviet influenced. The Czechoslovak avant-garde artistic movement known as the <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_style&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brussels style (page does not exist)">Brussels style</a> came up</i> in the time of political liberalization of Czechoslovakia in the 1960s. <a href="/wiki/Brutalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Brutalism">Brutalism</a> dominated in the 1970s and 1980s. </p>
      <p>The Czech Republic is not shying away from the more modern trends of international architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-architecture_169-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-architecture-169">[169]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Czech_literature" title="Czech literature">Czech literature</a>
      </div>
      <p>The literature from the area of today's Czech Republic was mostly written in Czech, but also in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> and German or even <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">Old Church Slavonic</a>. <a href="/wiki/Franz_Kafka" title="Franz Kafka">Franz Kafka</a>, who—while bilingual in Czech and German<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHawes200829_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHawes200829-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESayer1996164–210_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESayer1996164–210-173">[173]</a></sup>—wrote his works (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Trial" title="The Trial">The Trial</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Castle_(novel)" title="The Castle (novel)">The Castle</a></i>) in German. </p>
      <p>In the second half of the 13th century, the royal court in Prague became one of the centers of the German <a href="/wiki/Minnesang" title="Minnesang">Minnesang</a> and courtly literature. The Czech German-language literature can be seen in the first half of the 20th century. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bible_translations_into_Czech" title="Bible translations into Czech">Bible translations</a> played a role in the development of Czech literature. The oldest Czech translation of the <a href="/wiki/Psalms" title="Psalms">Psalms</a> originated in the late 13th century and the first complete Czech translation of the Bible was finished around 1360. The first complete printed Czech Bible was published in 1488. The first complete Czech Bible translation from the original languages was published between 1579 and 1593. The <a href="/wiki/Codex_Gigas" title="Codex Gigas">Codex Gigas</a> from the 12th century is the largest extant medieval manuscript in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Czech-language literature can be divided into several periods: the Middle Ages; the Hussite period; the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_humanism" title="Renaissance humanism">Renaissance humanism</a>; the Baroque period; the Enlightenment and Czech reawakening in the first half of the 19th century, modern literature in second half of the 19th century; the avant-garde of the interwar period; the years under Communism; and the Czech Republic. </p>
      <p>The antiwar comedy novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Soldier_%C5%A0vejk" title="The Good Soldier Švejk">The Good Soldier Švejk</a></i> is the most translated Czech book in history. </p>
      <p>The international literary award the <a href="/wiki/Franz_Kafka_Prize" title="Franz Kafka Prize">Franz Kafka Prize</a> is awarded in the Czech Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Czech Republic has the densest network of libraries in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Czech literature and culture played a role on at least two occasions when Czechs lived under oppression and political activity was suppressed. On both of these occasions, in the early 19th century and then again in the 1960s, the Czechs used their cultural and literary effort to strive for political freedom, establishing a confident, politically aware nation.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Czech_Lands" class="mw-redirect" title="Music of the Czech Lands">Music of the Czech Lands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moravian_traditional_music" title="Moravian traditional music">Moravian traditional music</a>
      </div>
      <p>The musical tradition of the Czech lands arose from first church hymns, whose first evidence is suggested at the break of 10th and 11th century. Some pieces of Czech music include two chorales, which in their time performed the function of anthems: "<a href="/wiki/Hospodine_pomiluj_ny" class="mw-redirect" title="Hospodine pomiluj ny">Lord, Have Mercy on Us</a>" and the <a href="/wiki/Hymn" title="Hymn">hymn</a> "<a href="/wiki/Saint_Wenceslas" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Wenceslas">Saint Wenceslas</a>" or "<a href="/wiki/Saint_Wenceslas_Chorale" title="Saint Wenceslas Chorale">Saint Wenceslas Chorale</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> The authorship of the anthem "Lord, Have Mercy on Us" is ascribed by some historians to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Adalbert_of_Prague" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Adalbert of Prague">Saint Adalbert of Prague</a> (sv.Vojtěch), bishop of <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, living between 956 and 997.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dvorak_Bedrich_Smetana_and_friends_in_1865.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Dvorak_Bedrich_Smetana_and_friends_in_1865.jpg/220px-Dvorak_Bedrich_Smetana_and_friends_in_1865.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Dvorak_Bedrich_Smetana_and_friends_in_1865.jpg/330px-Dvorak_Bedrich_Smetana_and_friends_in_1865.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Dvorak_Bedrich_Smetana_and_friends_in_1865.jpg/440px-Dvorak_Bedrich_Smetana_and_friends_in_1865.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="803"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dvorak_Bedrich_Smetana_and_friends_in_1865.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bed%C5%99ich_Smetana" title="Bedřich Smetana">Bedřich Smetana</a> on the painting of <a href="/wiki/Franti%C5%A1ek_Dvo%C5%99%C3%A1k_(painter)" title="František Dvořák (painter)">František Dvořák</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The wealth of musical culture lies in the classical music tradition during all historical periods, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">Baroque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Classical_period_(music)" title="Classical period (music)">Classicism</a>, Romantic, <a href="/wiki/Modernism_(music)" title="Modernism (music)">modern classical</a> music and in the <a href="/wiki/Traditional_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Traditional music">traditional</a> folk music of Bohemia, Moravia and <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a>. Since the early era of artificial music, Czech musicians and composers have been influenced the folk music of the region and dance. </p>
      <p>Czech music can be considered to have been "beneficial" in both the European and worldwide context, several times co-determined or even determined a newly arriving era in musical art,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> above all of <a href="/wiki/Classical_period_(music)" title="Classical period (music)">Classical</a> era, as well as by original attitudes in <a href="/wiki/Baroque_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Baroque (music)">Baroque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romantic_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Romantic (music)">Romantic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modern_classical" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern classical">modern classical</a> music. Some Czech musical works are <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bartered_Bride" title="The Bartered Bride">The Bartered Bride</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/New_World_Symphony" class="mw-redirect" title="New World Symphony">New World Symphony</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Sinfonietta_(Jan%C3%A1%C4%8Dek)" title="Sinfonietta (Janáček)">Sinfonietta</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Jen%C5%AFfa" title="Jenůfa">Jenůfa</a></i>. </p>
      <p>A music festival in the country is <a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring_International_Music_Festival" title="Prague Spring International Music Festival">Prague Spring International Music Festival</a> of classical music, a permanent showcase for performing artists, symphony orchestras and chamber music ensembles of the world. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">Theatre</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:331px;max-width:331px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:225px;max-width:225px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Narodni_Divadlo,_National_Theater,_Prague_-_8798.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Portrait" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Narodni_Divadlo%2C_National_Theater%2C_Prague_-_8798.jpg/223px-Narodni_Divadlo%2C_National_Theater%2C_Prague_-_8798.jpg" decoding="async" width="223" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Narodni_Divadlo%2C_National_Theater%2C_Prague_-_8798.jpg/335px-Narodni_Divadlo%2C_National_Theater%2C_Prague_-_8798.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Narodni_Divadlo%2C_National_Theater%2C_Prague_-_8798.jpg/446px-Narodni_Divadlo%2C_National_Theater%2C_Prague_-_8798.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4300" data-file-height="2892"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:102px;max-width:102px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Narodni_Divadlo,_Estates_Theater,_Prague_-_8604.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Portrait" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Narodni_Divadlo%2C_Estates_Theater%2C_Prague_-_8604.jpg/100px-Narodni_Divadlo%2C_Estates_Theater%2C_Prague_-_8604.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Narodni_Divadlo%2C_Estates_Theater%2C_Prague_-_8604.jpg/150px-Narodni_Divadlo%2C_Estates_Theater%2C_Prague_-_8604.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Narodni_Divadlo%2C_Estates_Theater%2C_Prague_-_8604.jpg/200px-Narodni_Divadlo%2C_Estates_Theater%2C_Prague_-_8604.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2912" data-file-height="4368"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          The <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_(Prague)" title="National Theatre (Prague)">National Theatre</a> (left) and the <a href="/wiki/Estates_Theatre" title="Estates Theatre">Estates Theatre</a> (right)
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Theatre_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Theatre of the Czech Republic">Theatre of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The roots of Czech theatre can be found in the Middle Ages, especially in cultural life of <a href="/wiki/Gothic_period" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic period">gothic period</a>. In the 19th century, the theatre played a role in the national awakening movement and later, in the 20th century it became a part of the modern European theatre art. Original Czech cultural phenomenon came into being at the end of the 1950s. This project called <a href="/wiki/Laterna_magika" class="mw-redirect" title="Laterna magika">Laterna magika</a>, resulting in productions that combined theater, dance and film in a poetic manner, considered the first <a href="/wiki/Multimedia_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Multimedia art">multimedia art</a> project in international context. </p>
      <p>A drama is <a href="/wiki/Karel_%C4%8Capek" title="Karel Čapek">Karel Čapek</a>'s play <i><a href="/wiki/R.U.R." title="R.U.R.">R.U.R.</a></i>, which introduced the word "<a href="/wiki/Robot" title="Robot">robot</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Cinema of the Czech Republic">Cinema of the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fabworldofjulesverne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Fabworldofjulesverne.jpg/160px-Fabworldofjulesverne.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Fabworldofjulesverne.jpg/240px-Fabworldofjulesverne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Fabworldofjulesverne.jpg/320px-Fabworldofjulesverne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1938" data-file-height="2951"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fabworldofjulesverne.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>American poster of Karel Zeman's 1958 film <i>A Deadly Invention</i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The tradition of Czech cinematography started in the second half of the 1890s. Peaks of the production in the era of silent movies include the historical drama <i>The Builder of the Temple</i> and the social and erotic drama <i>Erotikon</i> directed by <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Machat%C3%BD" title="Gustav Machatý">Gustav Machatý</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> The early Czech <a href="/wiki/Sound_film" title="Sound film">sound film</a> era was productive, above all in mainstream genres, with the comedies of <a href="/wiki/Martin_Fri%C4%8D" title="Martin Frič">Martin Frič</a> or <a href="/wiki/Karel_Lama%C4%8D" title="Karel Lamač">Karel Lamač</a>. There were dramatic movies sought internationally. </p>
      <p>After the period of Nazi occupation and early communist official dramaturgy of socialist realism in movies at the turn of the 1940s and 1950s with a fewer exceptions such as <i><a href="/wiki/Krakatit" title="Krakatit">Krakatit</a></i> or <i>Men without wings</i> (awarded by <a href="/wiki/Palme_d%27Or" title="Palme d'Or">Palme d'Or</a> in 1946), an era of the Czech film began with animated films, performed in anglophone countries under the name "The Fabulous World of Jules Verne" from 1958, which combined acted drama with animation, and <a href="/wiki/Ji%C5%99%C3%AD_Trnka" title="Jiří Trnka">Jiří Trnka</a>, the founder of the modern puppet film.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> This began a tradition of animated films (<i><a href="/wiki/Mole_(Zden%C4%9Bk_Miler_character)" title="Mole (Zdeněk Miler character)">Mole</a></i> etc.). </p>
      <p>In the 1960s, the hallmark of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_New_Wave" title="Czechoslovak New Wave">Czechoslovak New Wave</a>'s films were improvised <a href="/wiki/Dialogue" title="Dialogue">dialogues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_comedy" title="Black comedy">black</a> and <a href="/wiki/Absurdity" title="Absurdity">absurd</a> humor and the occupation of non-actors. Directors are trying to preserve natural atmosphere without refinement and artificial arrangement of scenes. A personality of the 1960s and the beginning of the 1970s with original manuscript and psychological impact is <a href="/wiki/Franti%C5%A1ek_Vl%C3%A1%C4%8Dil" title="František Vláčil">František Vláčil</a>. Another international author is <a href="/wiki/Jan_%C5%A0vankmajer" title="Jan Švankmajer">Jan Švankmajer</a>, a filmmaker and artist whose work spans several media. He is a self-labeled <a href="/wiki/Surrealism" title="Surrealism">surrealist</a> known for animations and features.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Barrandov_Studios" title="Barrandov Studios">Barrandov Studios</a> in Prague are the largest film studios with film locations in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> Filmmakers have come to <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> to shoot scenery no longer found in Berlin, Paris and Vienna. The city of <a href="/wiki/Karlovy_Vary" title="Karlovy Vary">Karlovy Vary</a> was used as a location for the 2006 James Bond film Casino Royale.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Czech_Lion" class="mw-redirect" title="Czech Lion">Czech Lion</a> is the highest Czech award for film achievement. <a href="/wiki/Karlovy_Vary_International_Film_Festival" title="Karlovy Vary International Film Festival">Karlovy Vary International Film Festival</a> is one of the film festivals that have been given competitive status by the <a href="/wiki/FIAPF" title="FIAPF">FIAPF</a>. Other film festivals held in the country include <a href="/wiki/Febiofest" title="Febiofest">Febiofest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jihlava_International_Documentary_Film_Festival" title="Jihlava International Documentary Film Festival">Jihlava International Documentary Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/One_World_Film_Festival" title="One World Film Festival">One World Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zl%C3%ADn_Film_Festival" title="Zlín Film Festival">Zlín Film Festival</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fresh_Film_Festival" title="Fresh Film Festival">Fresh Film Festival</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <p>Journalists and media enjoy a degree of <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom</a>. There are restrictions against writing in support of <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a>, racism or violating <a href="/wiki/Czech_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Czech law">Czech law</a>. The Czech press was ranked as the 23rd most free press in the World Freedom Index by <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a> in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe/Radio_Liberty" title="Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty">Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty</a> has its headquarters in Prague. </p>
      <p>The most watched main <a href="/wiki/News_program" title="News program">news program</a> is <a href="/wiki/TV_Nova_(Czech_Republic)" title="TV Nova (Czech Republic)">TV Nova</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> A news webpage in the Czech Republic is ct24.cz, which is owned by <a href="/wiki/Czech_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Czech Television">Czech Television</a> – the only national public television service – and its 24-hour news channel <a href="/wiki/%C4%8CT24" title="ČT24">ČT24</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> Other public services include the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Radio" title="Czech Radio">Czech Radio</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Czech_News_Agency" title="Czech News Agency">Czech News Agency</a> (ČTK). For privately owned television services, there is TV Nova, the most popular channel in the Czech Republic. </p>
      <p>The best-selling daily national newspapers are <a href="/wiki/Blesk" title="Blesk">Blesk</a> (average 1.15M daily readers), <a href="/wiki/Mlad%C3%A1_fronta_DNES" title="Mladá fronta DNES">Mladá fronta DNES</a> (average 752,000 daily readers), <a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%A1vo" title="Právo">Právo</a> (average 260,00 daily readers) and Deník (average 72,000 daily readers).<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Czech_cuisine" title="Czech cuisine">Czech cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pilsner_urquell_mug.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Pilsner_urquell_mug.jpg/220px-Pilsner_urquell_mug.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Pilsner_urquell_mug.jpg/330px-Pilsner_urquell_mug.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Pilsner_urquell_mug.jpg/440px-Pilsner_urquell_mug.jpg 2x" data-file-width="928" data-file-height="696"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pilsner_urquell_mug.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A mug of <a href="/wiki/Pilsner_Urquell" title="Pilsner Urquell">Pilsner Urquell</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Pilsner" title="Pilsner">pilsner</a> type of <a href="/wiki/Pale_lager" title="Pale lager">pale lager</a> beer, brewed since 1842
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Czech cuisine is marked by an emphasis on meat dishes with pork, beef and chicken. Goose, duck, rabbit and venison are served. Fish is less common, with the occasional exception of fresh <a href="/wiki/Trout" title="Trout">trout</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carp" title="Carp">carp</a>, which is served at Christmas. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Beer_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Beer in the Czech Republic">Czech beer</a> with the first brewery is known to have existed in 993 and the Czech Republic has the highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_beer_consumption_per_capita" title="List of countries by beer consumption per capita">beer consumption per capita</a> in the world. The "<a href="/wiki/Pilsner" title="Pilsner">pilsner</a> style beer" (pils) originated in <a href="/wiki/Plze%C5%88" title="Plzeň">Plzeň</a>, where the world's first-ever blond lager <a href="/wiki/Pilsner_Urquell" title="Pilsner Urquell">Pilsner Urquell</a> is still being produced, making it the inspiration for more than two-thirds of the beer produced in the world today. Further south the town of <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cesk%C3%A9_Bud%C4%9Bjovice" title="České Budějovice">České Budějovice</a>, lent its name to its beer, known as <a href="/wiki/Budweiser_Budvar" class="mw-redirect" title="Budweiser Budvar">Budweiser Budvar</a>. </p>
      <p>Tourism around the Southern Moravian region has been producing <a href="/wiki/Czech_wine" title="Czech wine">wine</a> since the Middle Ages; about 94% of <a href="/wiki/Vineyard" title="Vineyard">vineyards</a> in the Czech Republic are Moravian. Aside from <a href="/wiki/Slivovitz" title="Slivovitz">slivovitz</a>, Czech beer and wine, the Czechs also produce two <a href="/wiki/Liquor" title="Liquor">liquors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernet_Stock" title="Fernet Stock">Fernet Stock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Becherovka" title="Becherovka">Becherovka</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kofola" title="Kofola">Kofola</a> is a non-alcoholic domestic <a href="/wiki/Cola" title="Cola">cola</a> soft drink which competes with <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a>. </p>
      <p>There is also a variety of local sausages, wurst, pâtés, and smoked and cured meats. Czech desserts include a variety of whipped cream, chocolate, and fruit pastries and tarts, crêpes, creme desserts and cheese, poppy-seed-filled and other types of traditional cakes such as <i><a href="/wiki/Buchteln" title="Buchteln">buchty</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kolach" title="Kolach">koláče</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Apple_strudel" title="Apple strudel"><i>štrúdl</i></a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Sport in the Czech Republic">Sport in the Czech Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:HC_LEV_Record_O2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/HC_LEV_Record_O2.jpg/220px-HC_LEV_Record_O2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/HC_LEV_Record_O2.jpg/330px-HC_LEV_Record_O2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/HC_LEV_Record_O2.jpg/440px-HC_LEV_Record_O2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:HC_LEV_Record_O2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/O2_Arena_(Prague)" title="O2 Arena (Prague)">O2 Arena</a> in Prague is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_ice_hockey_arenas" title="List of European ice hockey arenas">second-largest ice hockey arena in Europe</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The most watched events in Czechia are <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey_at_the_Olympic_Games" title="Ice hockey at the Olympic Games">Olympic Ice hockey tournaments</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ice_Hockey_World_Championships" title="Ice Hockey World Championships">Ice Hockey Championships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> The two leading sports are <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>. Other most popular sports according to the size of the membership base of sports clubs include <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Floorball" title="Floorball">floorball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ball_hockey" title="Ball hockey">ball hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sport_of_athletics" title="Sport of athletics">athletics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country has won 14 gold medals in <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">summer</a> and five gold medals in <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">winter</a> <a href="/wiki/All-time_Olympic_Games_medal_table" title="All-time Olympic Games medal table">Olympic history</a>. <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Czech Republic men's national ice hockey team">The Czech ice hockey team</a> won the gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/1998_Winter_Olympics" title="1998 Winter Olympics">1998 Winter Olympics</a> and has won twelve gold medals at the <a href="/wiki/IHWC" class="mw-redirect" title="IHWC">World Championships</a>, including three straight from <a href="/wiki/1999_Men%27s_World_Ice_Hockey_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="1999 Men's World Ice Hockey Championships">1999</a> to <a href="/wiki/2001_Men%27s_World_Ice_Hockey_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="2001 Men's World Ice Hockey Championships">2001</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0koda_Motorsport" title="Škoda Motorsport">Škoda Motorsport</a> is engaged in <a href="/wiki/Motorsport" title="Motorsport">competition racing</a> since 1901, and has gained a number of titles with various vehicles around the world. <a href="/wiki/MTX_(automobile)" title="MTX (automobile)">MTX</a> automobile company was formerly engaged in the manufacture of <a href="/wiki/Auto_racing" title="Auto racing">racing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Formula_racing" title="Formula racing">formula</a> cars since 1969. </p>
      <p>A sport done here is hiking. The word for "tourist" in the Czech language, <i>turista</i>, also means "trekker" or "hiker". For hikers, thanks to the more than 120-year-old tradition, there is a <a href="/wiki/Czech_Hiking_Markers_System" title="Czech Hiking Markers System">Czech Hiking Markers System</a> of <a href="/wiki/Trail_blazing" title="Trail blazing">trail blazing</a>, that has been adopted by countries worldwide. There is a network of around 40,000&nbsp;km of marked short- and long-distance trails crossing the whole country and all the Czech mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> </p>

        <li id="cite_note-languages-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-languages_2-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Citizens belonging to minorities, which traditionally and on a long-term basis live within the territory of the Czech Republic, enjoy the right to use their language in communication with authorities and in courts of law (for the list of recognized minorities see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.vlada.cz/en/pracovni-a-poradni-organy-vlady/rnm/historie-a-soucasnost-rady-en-16666/">National Minorities Policy of the Government of the Czech Republic</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120607051111/http://www.vlada.cz/en/pracovni-a-poradni-organy-vlady/rnm/historie-a-soucasnost-rady-en-16666/">Archived</a> 7 June 2012 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>, Belarusian and Vietnamese since 4 July 2013, see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://zpravy.idnes.cz/vietnamci-oficialni-narodnostni-mensinou-fiq-/domaci.aspx?c=A130703_133019_domaci_jj">Česko má nové oficiální národnostní menšiny. Vietnamce a Bělorusy</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130708074104/http://zpravy.idnes.cz/vietnamci-oficialni-narodnostni-mensinou-fiq-/domaci.aspx?c=A130703_133019_domaci_jj">Archived</a> 8 July 2013 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>). Article 25 of the Czech <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_and_Basic_Freedoms" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights and Basic Freedoms">Charter of Fundamental Rights and Basic Freedoms</a> ensures the right of the national and ethnic minorities to education and communication with the authorities in their own language. Act No. 500/2004 Coll. (<i>The Administrative Rule</i>) in its paragraph 16 (4) (<i>Procedural Language</i>) ensures that a citizen of the Czech Republic who belongs to a national or an ethnic minority, which traditionally and on a long-term basis lives within the territory of the Czech Republic, has the right to address an administrative agency and proceed before it in the language of the minority. If the administrative agency has no employee with knowledge of the language, the agency is bound to obtain a translator at the agency's own expense. According to Act No. 273/2001 (<i>Concerning the Rights of Members of Minorities</i>) paragraph 9 (<i>The right to use language of a national minority in dealing with authorities and in front of the courts of law</i>) the same also applies to members of national minorities in the courts of law.</span> </li>
